**Kuala Lumpur** ,^[\[a\]](#cite_note-8)^ officially the **Federal Territory of Kuala Lumpur** ,^[\[b\]](#cite_note-9)^ and colloquially referred to as **KL** , is the [capital city](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") and a [federal territory](/wiki/Federal_Territories_of_Malaysia "Federal Territories of Malaysia") of [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia"). It is the largest city in the country, covering an area of 243 km^2^ (94 sq mi) with a census population of 2,075,600 as of 2024^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit)^.^[\[8\]](#cite_note-10)^ [Greater Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Greater_Kuala_Lumpur "Greater Kuala Lumpur"), also known as the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley"), is an [urban agglomeration](/wiki/Urban_agglomeration "Urban agglomeration") of 8.8 million people as of 2024. It is among the fastest growing metropolitan regions in [Southeast Asia](/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"), both in population and economic development.{#cite_ref-10}

The city serves as the cultural, financial, tourism, political and economic centre of Malaysia. It is also home to the [bicameral](/wiki/Bicameral "Bicameral") [Parliament of Malaysia](/wiki/Parliament_of_Malaysia "Parliament of Malaysia") (consisting of the [Dewan Rakyat](/wiki/Dewan_Rakyat "Dewan Rakyat") and the [Dewan Negara](/wiki/Dewan_Negara "Dewan Negara")) and the [Istana Negara](/wiki/Istana_Negara,_Jalan_Tuanku_Abdul_Halim "Istana Negara, Jalan Tuanku Abdul Halim"), the official residence of the [Yang di-Pertuan Agong](/wiki/Yang_di-Pertuan_Agong "Yang di-Pertuan Agong") (monarch of Malaysia). Kuala Lumpur was first developed around 1857 as a town serving the [tin mines](/wiki/Tin_mining "Tin mining") of the region, and important figures such as [Yap Ah Loy](/wiki/Yap_Ah_Loy "Yap Ah Loy") and [Frank Swettenham](/wiki/Frank_Swettenham "Frank Swettenham") were instrumental in the early development of the city during the late 19th century. It served as the capital of [Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor") from 1880 until 1978. Kuala Lumpur was the founding capital of the [Federation of Malaya](/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya "Federation of Malaya") and its successor, Malaysia. The city remained the seat of the executive and judicial branches of the [Malaysian federal government](/wiki/Malaysian_federal_government "Malaysian federal government") until these were relocated to [Putrajaya](/wiki/Putrajaya "Putrajaya") in early 1999.^[\[9\]](#cite_note-11)^ However, some sections of the political bodies still remain in Kuala Lumpur. The city is one of the three [Federal Territories of Malaysia](/wiki/Federal_Territories_of_Malaysia "Federal Territories of Malaysia"),^[\[10\]](#cite_note-Ibrahim,_2007-12)^ [enclaved](/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave "Enclave and exclave") within the state of [Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor"), on the central west coast of [Peninsular Malaysia](/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia "Peninsular Malaysia").^[\[11\]](#cite_note-13)^{#cite_ref-13}

Since the 1990s, the city has played host to many international sporting, political and cultural events, including the [1998 Commonwealth Games](/wiki/1998_Commonwealth_Games "1998 Commonwealth Games"), [2001 Southeast Asian Games](/wiki/2001_Southeast_Asian_Games "2001 Southeast Asian Games"), [2017 Southeast Asian Games](/wiki/2017_Southeast_Asian_Games "2017 Southeast Asian Games"), [Formula One](/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One"), [Moto GP](/wiki/Moto_GP "Moto GP") and [FIFA World Youth Championships](/wiki/FIFA_Youth_Championship "FIFA Youth Championship"). Kuala Lumpur has undergone rapid development in recent decades and is home to the [tallest twin buildings](/wiki/List_of_tallest_twin_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world "List of tallest twin buildings and structures in the world") in the world, the [Petronas Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers") which have since become an iconic symbol of Malaysian development. Kuala Lumpur is well connected with neighbouring urban metro regions such as [Petaling Jaya](/wiki/Petaling_Jaya "Petaling Jaya") via the rapidly expanding [Klang Valley Integrated Transit System](/wiki/Klang_Valley_Integrated_Transit_System "Klang Valley Integrated Transit System"). Residents of the city can also travel to other parts of [Peninsular Malaysia](/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia "Peninsular Malaysia") as well as to [Kuala Lumpur International Airport](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_International_Airport "Kuala Lumpur International Airport") (KLIA) via rail through [KL Sentral](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Sentral_station "Kuala Lumpur Sentral station").

Kuala Lumpur was ranked the 6th most-visited city in the world on the Mastercard Destination Cities Index in 2019.^[\[12\]](#cite_note-14)^ The city houses three of the world's ten largest shopping malls.^[\[13\]](#cite_note-15)^ Kuala Lumpur ranks 70th in the world and the second in Southeast Asia after [Singapore](/wiki/Singapore "Singapore") for the [Economist Intelligence Unit](/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit "Economist Intelligence Unit")'s [Global Liveability Ranking](/wiki/Global_Liveability_Ranking "Global Liveability Ranking")^[\[14\]](#cite_note-16)^ and ninth in ASPAC and second in Southeast Asia after Singapore for [KPMG](/wiki/KPMG "KPMG")'s Leading Technology Innovation Hub 2021.^[\[15\]](#cite_note-17)^ Kuala Lumpur was named [World Book Capital](/wiki/World_Book_Capital "World Book Capital") 2020 by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO").^[\[16\]](#cite_note-18)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-19)^ In 2024, Kuala Lumpur was ranked second for the best outstanding city in Southeast Asia, after Singapore, and 135th in the world by the [Oxford Economic Papers](/wiki/Oxford_Economic_Papers "Oxford Economic Papers")' Global Cities Index.{#cite_ref-19}  

Etymology {#Etymology}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Etymology")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Masjid_Jamek_along_Klang_%26_Gombak_River_%28220512%29_06.jpg/240px-Masjid_Jamek_along_Klang_%26_Gombak_River_%28220512%29_06.jpg)](/wiki/File:Masjid_Jamek_along_Klang_%26_Gombak_River_(220512)_06.jpg) [Jamek Mosque](/wiki/Jamek_Mosque "Jamek Mosque") at the confluence of the [Gombak](/wiki/Gombak_River "Gombak River") (left) and [Klang](/wiki/Klang_River "Klang River") (right) rivers. The earliest settlement of Kuala Lumpur developed on the eastern side of the river bank (to the right in this picture).

Kuala Lumpur means "muddy confluence" in [Malay](/wiki/Malay_language "Malay language"); *Kuala* is the point where two rivers join or an [estuary](/wiki/Estuary "Estuary"), and *lumpur* means "mud".^[\[18\]](#cite_note-20)^^[\[19\]](#cite_note-21)^^[\[20\]](#cite_note-22)^ One suggestion is that it was named after Sungai Lumpur ("muddy river"); in the 1820s a place named *Sungei Lumpoor* was said to be the most important tin-producing settlement up the [Klang River](/wiki/Klang_River "Klang River").^[\[21\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick20001–2-23)^ However, Kuala Lumpur lies at the confluence of [Gombak River](/wiki/Gombak_River "Gombak River") and Klang River and therefore should be named Kuala Gombak, since the *kuala* is typically named after the river that joins a larger river or the sea.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195511-24)^ Some have argued that Sungai Lumpur extended to the confluence. Therefore the point where it joined the Klang River would be Kuala Lumpur,^[\[23\]](#cite_note-sutanpuasa-25)^ Although this Sungai Lumpur is said to be another river joining the Klang River 1.5 kilometres (1 mile) upstream from the Gombak confluence, or perhaps located to the north of the [Batu Caves](/wiki/Batu_Caves "Batu Caves") area.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195511-24)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGullick195511_24-1}

It has also been proposed that Kuala Lumpur was originally named Pengkalan Lumpur ("muddy landing place") in the same way that [Klang](/wiki/Klang_(city) "Klang (city)") was once called Pengkalan Batu ("stone landing place"), but became corrupted into Kuala Lumpur.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-sutanpuasa-25)^ Another theory says that it was initially a [Cantonese](/wiki/Cantonese "Cantonese") word *lam-pa* , meaning 'flooded jungle' or 'decayed jungle'. There is no firm contemporary evidence for these suggestions other than anecdotes.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-26)^ The name may also be a corrupted form of an earlier forgotten name.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195511-24)^{#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGullick195511_24-2}  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: History")\]  
Main article: [History of Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/History_of_Kuala_Lumpur "History of Kuala Lumpur")  

### Early years {#Early_years}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Early years")\]  
Historical affiliations
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Selangor_%28pre_1965%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Selangor_%28pre_1965%29.svg.png) [Sultanate of Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor") 1857--1974  
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_Malaya_%281896%E2%80%931950%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaya_%281896%E2%80%931950%29.svg.png) [Federated Malay States](/wiki/Federated_Malay_States "Federated Malay States") 1895--1942; 1945--1946  
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Japan_%281870%E2%80%931999%29.svg/22px-Flag_of_Japan_%281870%E2%80%931999%29.svg.png) [Empire of Japan](/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Malaya "Japanese occupation of Malaya") 1942--1945  
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Flag_of_Malaya_%281896%E2%80%931950%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaya_%281896%E2%80%931950%29.svg.png) [Malayan Union](/wiki/Malayan_Union "Malayan Union") 1946--1948  
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Flag_of_Malaya_%281950%E2%80%931963%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaya_%281950%E2%80%931963%29.svg.png) [Federation of Malaya](/wiki/Federation_of_Malaya "Federation of Malaya") 1948--1963  
> ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flag_of_Malaysia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malaysia.svg.png) [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia") 1963--present

Some consider Kuala Lumpur to have been founded by the Malay Chief of [Klang](/wiki/Klang,_Malaysia "Klang, Malaysia"), Raja Abdullah, who sent [Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_people "Chinese people") miners into the region to open tin mines in 1857,^[\[25\]](#cite_note-27)^ although it is unclear who the first settlers were since there were likely settlements at the Gombak-Klang river confluence before that in the 1820s.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-Fatt2011-28)^ Chinese miners were known to be involved in tin mining up the [Selangor River](/wiki/Selangor_River "Selangor River") in the 1840s about 16 kilometres (10 miles) north of present-day Kuala Lumpur,^[\[27\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195510–11-29)^ and [Mandailing](/wiki/Mandailing "Mandailing") Sumatrans led by [Raja Asal](/w/index.php?title=Raja_Asal&action=edit&redlink=1 "Raja Asal (page does not exist)") \[[ms](https://ms.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raja_Asal "ms:Raja Asal")\] and Sutan Puasa were also involved in tin mining and trade in the [Ulu Klang](/wiki/Ulu_Klang "Ulu Klang") region before 1860, and Sumatrans may have settled in the upper reaches of Klang River in the first quarter of the 19th century, or possibly earlier.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-sutanpuasa-25)^^[\[28\]](#cite_note-gulllick_3-30)^^[\[29\]](#cite_note-31)^^[\[26\]](#cite_note-Fatt2011-28)^ Kuala Lumpur was originally a small hamlet of just a few houses and shops at the confluence of the [Sungai Gombak](/wiki/Sungai_Gombak "Sungai Gombak") and Sungai Klang ([Klang River](/wiki/Klang_River "Klang River")). Kuala Lumpur became established as a town  1857,^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^ when Raja Abdullah bin Raja Jaafar, aided by his brother Raja Juma'at of [Lukut](/wiki/Lukut "Lukut"), raised funds from [Malaccan](/wiki/Malacca "Malacca") Chinese businessmen to hire Chinese miners from [Lukut](/wiki/Lukut "Lukut") to open new [tin](/wiki/Tin "Tin") mines there.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-33)^^[\[32\]](#cite_note-34)^ The miners landed at Kuala Lumpur and continued on foot to [Ampang](/wiki/Ampang,_Kuala_Lumpur "Ampang, Kuala Lumpur"), where they opened the first mine.^[\[33\]](#cite_note-35)^ Kuala Lumpur was the furthest point up the Klang River to which supplies could conveniently be brought by boat and therefore became a collection and dispersal point serving the tin mines.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195510-36)^^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^{#cite_ref-ooi_32-1}  
[![Yap Ah Loy](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Yap_Ah_Loy.jpg/110px-Yap_Ah_Loy.jpg)](/wiki/File:Yap_Ah_Loy.jpg)  
Kapitan [Yap Ah Loy](/wiki/Yap_Ah_Loy "Yap Ah Loy"), the third Chinese Kapitan of Kuala Lumpur  
[![Frank Swettenham](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sir_frank_swettenham.gif/122px-Sir_frank_swettenham.gif)](/wiki/File:Sir_frank_swettenham.gif)  
[Frank Swettenham](/wiki/Frank_Swettenham "Frank Swettenham"),   
credited with Kuala Lumpur's rapid growth and development

Despite a high death toll from the [malarial](/wiki/Malaria "Malaria") conditions of the jungle, the Ampang mines succeeded and exported the first tin in 1859.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick195510-36)^ At that time, Sutan Puasa was already trading near Ampang. Two traders from Lukut, Hiu Siew and Yap Ah Sze, arrived in Kuala Lumpur and set up shops to sell provisions to miners in exchange for tin.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-37)^^[\[36\]](#cite_note-38)^ The town, spurred on by tin-mining, started to develop around Old Market Square ([Medan Pasar](/wiki/Medan_Pasar_Besar "Medan Pasar Besar")), with roads radiating out towards Ampang as well as [Pudu](/wiki/Pudu,_Kuala_Lumpur "Pudu, Kuala Lumpur") and [Batu](/wiki/Batu,_Kuala_Lumpur "Batu, Kuala Lumpur") (the destinations became the names of these roads: [Ampang Road](/wiki/Jalan_Ampang "Jalan Ampang"), [Pudu Road](/wiki/Jalan_Pudu "Jalan Pudu"), and [Batu Road](/wiki/Batu_Road "Batu Road")), where miners had also begun to settle in, and [Petaling](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street") and [Damansara](/wiki/Damansara,_Selangor "Damansara, Selangor").^[\[37\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick20007–9-39)^ The miners formed gangs^[\[38\]](#cite_note-kiat-40)^ and the gangs frequently fought in this period, particularly factions of Kuala Lumpur and Kanching, mainly over control of the best tin mines.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Gullick2-41)^ Leaders of the Chinese community were conferred the title of [Kapitan Cina](/wiki/Kapitan_Cina "Kapitan Cina") (Chinese headman) by the Malay chief, and Hiu Siew, the early Chinese trader, became the first Kapitan of Kuala Lumpur.^[\[40\]](#cite_note-42)^ The third Chinese Kapitan of Kuala Lumpur, [Yap Ah Loy](/wiki/Yap_Ah_Loy "Yap Ah Loy"), was appointed in 1868.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-Fatt2011-28)^{#cite_ref-Fatt2011_28-2}

Important Malay figures of early Kuala Lumpur also included Haji Mohamed Tahir, who became the Dato Dagang ("chief of traders").^[\[28\]](#cite_note-gulllick_3-30)^ The [Minangkabaus](/wiki/Minangkabau_people "Minangkabau people") of Sumatra became another important group who [traded](/wiki/Minangkabau_businesspeople "Minangkabau businesspeople") and established tobacco plantations in the area.^[\[41\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick200021-43)^ Notable Minangkabaus included their headman, Dato' Sati, Utsman Abdullah,^[\[42\]](#cite_note-44)^ and [Haji Mohamed Taib](/wiki/Mohamed_Taib_bin_Haji_Abdul_Samad "Mohamed Taib bin Haji Abdul Samad"), who was involved in the early development of [Kampung Baru](/wiki/Kampung_Baru,_Kuala_Lumpur "Kampung Baru, Kuala Lumpur").^[\[43\]](#cite_note-45)^^[\[44\]](#cite_note-46)^ The Minangkabaus were also significant socio-religious figures, for example Utsman bin Abdullah was the first [kadi](/wiki/Qadi "Qadi") of Kuala Lumpur, as well as Muhammad Nur bin Ismail.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-47)^{#cite_ref-47}  

### Beginning of modern Kuala Lumpur {#Beginning_of_modern_Kuala_Lumpur}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Beginning of modern Kuala Lumpur")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Panorama_of_Kuala_Lumpur_ca._1884.jpg/370px-Panorama_of_Kuala_Lumpur_ca._1884.jpg)](/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Kuala_Lumpur_ca._1884.jpg) Part of a panoramic view of Kuala Lumpur  1884. To the left is the [Padang](/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Kuala_Lumpur "Merdeka Square, Kuala Lumpur"). The buildings were constructed of wood and [atap](/wiki/Attap_dwelling "Attap dwelling") before regulations enacted by Swettenham in 1884 required buildings to use bricks and tiles. The appearance of Kuala Lumpur transformed rapidly in the following years due to the building regulations.

Early Kuala Lumpur was a small town that suffered from many social and political problems -- the buildings were made of wood and '[atap](/wiki/Nypa_fruticans "Nypa fruticans")' (palm frond [thatching](/wiki/Thatching "Thatching")). The buildings were prone to catching fire, and due to a lack of proper sanitation, the town was plagued with diseases. It also suffered from a constant threat of flooding due to its location. The town became embroiled in the [Selangor Civil War](/wiki/Selangor_Civil_War "Selangor Civil War") in part over control of revenue from the tin mines. Yap Ah Loy allied himself with [Tengku Kudin](/w/index.php?title=Tengku_Kudin&action=edit&redlink=1 "Tengku Kudin (page does not exist)") \[[ms](https://ms.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tengku_Kudin "ms:Tengku Kudin")\] and the [Hai San](/wiki/Hai_San_Secret_Society "Hai San Secret Society") secret society, they fought against a rival secret society, [Ghee Hin](/wiki/Ghee_Hin_Kongsi "Ghee Hin Kongsi"), who allied themselves with Raja Mahdi.^[\[46\]](#cite_note-48)^ Raja Asal and Sutan Puasa switched sides to Raja Mahdi, and Kuala Lumpur was captured in 1872 and burnt to the ground. Yap escaped to Klang where he assembled another fighting force and recaptured Kuala Lumpur in March 1873, defeating Raja Mahdi's forces with the help of fighters from [Pahang](/wiki/Pahang "Pahang").^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Gullick2-41)^ The war and other setbacks, such as dropping tin prices, led to a slump. A major outbreak of [cholera](/wiki/Cholera "Cholera") caused many to flee. The slump lasted until late 1879, when rising prices for tin allowed the town to recover.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^ In late 1881, the town was severely flooded, after a fire that had destroyed the entire town in January. With the town being rebuilt a few times and having thrived, this was due in large to Yap Ah Loy.^[\[47\]](#cite_note-49)^^[\[48\]](#cite_note-virtual-50)^ Yap, together with [Frank Swettenham](/wiki/Frank_Swettenham "Frank Swettenham") who was appointed the [Resident](/wiki/Resident_(title) "Resident (title)") in 1882, were the two most important figures of early Kuala Lumpur with Swettenham credited with its rapid growth and development and its transformation into a major urban centre.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-Britannica-51)^{#cite_ref-Britannica_51-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/KITLV_-_3652_-_Lambert_%26_Co.%2C_G.R._-_Singapore_-_Governmental_Office_at_Kuala_Lumpur_in_Selangor_-_circa_1900.tif/lossy-page1-240px-KITLV_-_3652_-_Lambert_%26_Co.%2C_G.R._-_Singapore_-_Governmental_Office_at_Kuala_Lumpur_in_Selangor_-_circa_1900.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:KITLV_-_3652_-_Lambert_%26_Co.,_G.R._-_Singapore_-_Governmental_Office_at_Kuala_Lumpur_in_Selangor_-_circa_1900.tif) The Government Offices of the [Federated Malay States](/wiki/Federated_Malay_States "Federated Malay States") (Now the [Sultan Abdul Samad Building](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building "Sultan Abdul Samad Building")) facing the [Padang](/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Kuala_Lumpur "Merdeka Square, Kuala Lumpur"),  1900

The early Chinese and Malay settled along the east bank of the Klang River. The Chinese mainly settled around the commercial centre of Market Square. The Malays, and later Indian [Chettiars](/wiki/Chettiar "Chettiar") and Muslims, resided in the Java Street area, now [Jalan Tun Perak](/wiki/Jalan_Tun_Perak "Jalan Tun Perak"). In 1880, the colonial administration moved the state capital of Selangor from Klang to the more strategically advantageous Kuala Lumpur, and British Resident [William Bloomfield Douglas](/wiki/William_Bloomfield_Douglas "William Bloomfield Douglas") decided to locate the government buildings and living quarters to the west of the river. Government offices and a new [police headquarters](/wiki/Royal_Malaysia_Police "Royal Malaysia Police") were built on [Bukit Aman](/wiki/Bukit_Aman "Bukit Aman"), and the Padang was initially created for police training.^[\[50\]](#cite_note-52)^ The Padang, now known as [Merdeka Square](/wiki/Dataran_Merdeka "Dataran Merdeka"), would later become the centre of the British administrative offices when the colonial government offices moved to the [Sultan Abdul Samad Building](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building "Sultan Abdul Samad Building") in 1897.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-virtual-50)^{#cite_ref-virtual_50-1}

[Frank Swettenham](/wiki/Frank_Swettenham "Frank Swettenham"), on becoming the British Resident, began improving the town by cleaning up the streets. He also stipulated in 1884 that buildings should be constructed of brick and tile so that they would be less flammable, and that the town be rebuilt with wider streets to reduce fire risk.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-Britannica-51)^^[\[51\]](#cite_note-53)^ [Kapitan](/wiki/Kapitan_Cina "Kapitan Cina") Yap Ah Loy bought a sprawling piece of real estate to set up a brick factory for the rebuilding of Kuala Lumpur, the [eponymous](/wiki/Eponymous "Eponymous") [Brickfields](/wiki/Brickfields,_Kuala_Lumpur "Brickfields, Kuala Lumpur").^[\[52\]](#cite_note-54)^ Demolished *atap* buildings were replaced with brick and tile buildings, and many of the new brick buildings had "[five-foot ways](/wiki/Five-foot_way "Five-foot way")" and Chinese carpentry work. This resulted in a distinct eclectic [shop house](/wiki/Shop_house "Shop house") architecture typical to this region. Kapitan Yap Ah Loy expanded road access, linking tin mines with the city with the main arterial routes of the present [Ampang Road](/wiki/Jalan_Ampang "Jalan Ampang"), [Pudu Road](/wiki/Jalan_Pudu "Jalan Pudu") and [Petaling Street](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street").^[\[53\]](#cite_note-55)^ As Chinese Kapitan, he held wide powers on a par with [Malay](/wiki/Malays_(ethnic_group) "Malays (ethnic group)") community leaders. Law reforms were implemented and new legal measures were introduced to the assembly. Yap also presided over a [small claims court](/wiki/Small_claims_court "Small claims court"). With a police force of six, he was able to uphold the rule of law, constructing a prison that could accommodate sixty prisoners at a time. Yap Ah Loy also built Kuala Lumpur's first school and a major tapioca mill in [Petaling Street](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street"), in which the Selangor's [Sultan Abdul Samad](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad "Sultan Abdul Samad") held an interest.^[\[54\]](#cite_note-56)^{#cite_ref-56}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/KITLV_-_79944_-_Kleingrothe%2C_C.J._-_Medan_-_Headquarters_of_the_F.M.S._Railways_at_Kuala_Lumpur_-_circa_1910.tif/lossy-page1-240px-KITLV_-_79944_-_Kleingrothe%2C_C.J._-_Medan_-_Headquarters_of_the_F.M.S._Railways_at_Kuala_Lumpur_-_circa_1910.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:KITLV_-_79944_-_Kleingrothe,_C.J._-_Medan_-_Headquarters_of_the_F.M.S._Railways_at_Kuala_Lumpur_-_circa_1910.tif) The construction of railway spurred the growth of the city. The first headquarters of the [Federated Malay States Railways](/wiki/Federated_Malay_States_Railways "Federated Malay States Railways") (now the [National Textile Museum](/wiki/National_Textile_Museum "National Textile Museum")) near the F.M.S. Government Offices in the distance,  1910.

A [railway line](/wiki/Port_Klang_Line "Port Klang Line") between Kuala Lumpur and Klang, initiated by Swettenham and completed in 1886, increased access and resulted in rapid growth. The population grew from 4,500 in 1884 to 20,000 in 1890.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^ As development intensified in the 1880s, putting pressure on sanitation, waste disposal and other health measures. A Sanitary Board created on 14 May 1890 was responsible for sanitation, road upkeep, street lighting, and other functions. This would eventually become the [Kuala Lumpur Municipal Council](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Hall "Kuala Lumpur City Hall") in 1948.^[\[55\]](#cite_note-57)^ In 1896, Kuala Lumpur was chosen as the capital of the newly formed [Federated Malay States](/wiki/Federated_Malay_States "Federated Malay States").^[\[56\]](#cite_note-58)^{#cite_ref-58}  

### 20th century--present {#20th_century.E2.80.93present}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: 20th century–present")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/An_arcade_of_shops_with_a_road_sweeper_at_work_in_the_street_of_Kuala_Lumpur%2C_1915-1925.jpg/220px-An_arcade_of_shops_with_a_road_sweeper_at_work_in_the_street_of_Kuala_Lumpur%2C_1915-1925.jpg)](/wiki/File:An_arcade_of_shops_with_a_road_sweeper_at_work_in_the_street_of_Kuala_Lumpur,_1915-1925.jpg) An arcade of [shophouses](/wiki/Shophouse "Shophouse") with a road sweeper at work in the street of Kuala Lumpur,  1915--1925.

Kuala Lumpur expanded considerably in the 20th century. It was 0.65 km^2^ (0.25 sq mi) in 1895, but was extended to encompass 20 km^2^ (7.7 sq mi) in 1903, and to 52 km^2^ (20 sq mi) by 1924. By the time it became a municipality in 1948 it had expanded to 93 km^2^ (36 sq mi), and then to 243 km^2^ (94 sq mi) in 1974 as a Federal Territory.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-reassessment-59)^^[\[58\]](#cite_note-60)^{#cite_ref-60}

Until 1974, Kuala Lumpur was one of the seven districts of Selangor (six before 1960).^[\[59\]](#cite_note-61)^ The Kuala Lumpur district comprises eight mukims -- [Sungai Buloh](/wiki/Sungai_Buloh "Sungai Buloh"), [Batu](/wiki/Mukim_Batu "Mukim Batu"), [Petaling](/wiki/Sri_Petaling "Sri Petaling"), [Ampang](/wiki/Ampang_Jaya "Ampang Jaya"), [Ulu Klang](/wiki/Ulu_Klang "Ulu Klang"), Kuala Lumpur (city and suburban) and [Setapak](/wiki/Setapak "Setapak").^[\[60\]](#cite_note-62)^{#cite_ref-62}

The development of a [rubber](/wiki/Natural_rubber "Natural rubber") industry in [Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor") fuelled by the demand for car tyres in the early 20th century led to a boom, and the population of Kuala Lumpur increased from 30,000 in 1900 to 80,000 in 1920.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-gullick_3-63)^ The commercial activities of Kuala Lumpur had been run to a large extent by Chinese businessmen such as [Loke Yew](/wiki/Loke_Yew "Loke Yew"), who was then the richest and most influential Chinese in Kuala Lumpur. The growth of the rubber industry led to an influx of foreign capital and planters, with new companies and industries becoming established in Kuala Lumpur, and other companies previously based elsewhere also found a presence here.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-gullick_3-63)^{#cite_ref-gullick_3_63-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Japanese_troops_mopping_up_in_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg/219px-Japanese_troops_mopping_up_in_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg)](/wiki/File:Japanese_troops_mopping_up_in_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg) Japanese troops advancing up High Street (now [Jalan Tun H S Lee](/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Kuala_Lumpur "List of roads in Kuala Lumpur")) in Kuala Lumpur in December 1941 during World War II.

During [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), Kuala Lumpur was [captured](/wiki/Battle_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Battle of Kuala Lumpur") by the [Imperial Japanese Army](/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army "Imperial Japanese Army") on 11 January 1942. Despite suffering little damage during the battle, the wartime occupation of the city resulted in significant loss of lives; at least 5,000 Chinese were killed in Kuala Lumpur in just a few weeks of occupation by Japanese forces, and thousands of Indians were sent as [forced labour](/wiki/Forced_labour "Forced labour") to work on the [Burma Railway](/wiki/Burma_Railway "Burma Railway") where many died.^[\[62\]](#cite_note-64)^ They occupied the city until 15 August 1945, when the commander in chief of the [Japanese Seventh Area Army](/wiki/Japanese_Seventh_Area_Army "Japanese Seventh Area Army") in Singapore and Malaysia, [Seishirō Itagaki](/wiki/Seishir%C5%8D_Itagaki "Seishirō Itagaki"), [surrendered](/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan "Surrender of Japan") to the British administration following the [atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki](/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki").^[\[63\]](#cite_note-65)^ Kuala Lumpur grew during the war, and continued after the war during the [Malayan Emergency (1948--1960)](/wiki/Malayan_Emergency "Malayan Emergency"), during which Malaya was preoccupied with a [communist](/wiki/Communism "Communism") insurgency and [New Villages](/wiki/New_Village "New Village") were established on the outskirts of the city.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-Britannica-51)^{#cite_ref-Britannica_51-2}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/KUALA_LUMPUR.png/220px-KUALA_LUMPUR.png)](/wiki/File:KUALA_LUMPUR.png) Map of Kuala Lumpur in 1951

The first municipal election in Kuala Lumpur was held on 16 February 1952. An *ad hoc* alliance between the Malay [UMNO](/wiki/UMNO "UMNO") and Chinese [MCA](/wiki/Malayan_Chinese_Association "Malayan Chinese Association") party candidates won a majority of the seats, and this led to the formation of the [Alliance Party](/wiki/Alliance_Party_(Malaysia) "Alliance Party (Malaysia)") (later the [Barisan Nasional](/wiki/Barisan_Nasional "Barisan Nasional")).^[\[64\]](#cite_note-ency-66)^ On 31 August 1957, the Federation of Malaya gained its independence from British rule.^[\[65\]](#cite_note-67)^ The British flag was lowered and the Malayan flag raised for the first time at the Padang at midnight on 30 August 1957,^[\[66\]](#cite_note-lam-68)^ and on the morning of 31 August, the ceremony for the [Declaration of Independence](/wiki/Malayan_Declaration_of_Independence "Malayan Declaration of Independence") was held at the [Merdeka Stadium](/wiki/Merdeka_Stadium "Merdeka Stadium") by the first Prime Minister of Malaya, [Tunku Abdul Rahman](/wiki/Tunku_Abdul_Rahman "Tunku Abdul Rahman"). Kuala Lumpur remained the capital after the [formation of Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia_Day "Malaysia Day") on 16 September 1963. The [Malaysian Houses of Parliament](/wiki/Malaysian_Houses_of_Parliament "Malaysian Houses of Parliament") were completed at the edge of the [Lake Gardens](/wiki/Lake_Gardens,_Kuala_Lumpur "Lake Gardens, Kuala Lumpur") in 1963.^[\[67\]](#cite_note-69)^ The population of Kuala Lumpur expanded considerably from 1960 to 2018, doubling in size every 13 years.^[\[68\]](#cite_note-70)^{#cite_ref-70}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/04/Majestic_Theatre_Pudu_Road.jpg/220px-Majestic_Theatre_Pudu_Road.jpg)](/wiki/File:Majestic_Theatre_Pudu_Road.jpg) The Majestic Theatre on Pudu Road was an early pioneer in Kuala Lumpur's cinema scene. It was converted into an amusement park in the 1990s and demolished in 2009.

Kuala Lumpur has seen several civil disturbances over the years. A riot in 1897 was a relatively minor affair that began with the confiscation of faulty *dacing* (a scale used by traders), and in 1912, a more serious disturbance called the *[tauchang](/wiki/Queue_(hairstyle) "Queue (hairstyle)")* riot began during the [Chinese New Year](/wiki/Chinese_New_Year "Chinese New Year") with the cutting of pigtails and ended with rioting and factional fighting lasting several days.^[\[69\]](#cite_note-71)^ The worst rioting on record in Malaysia, however, occurred on 13 May 1969, when race riots broke out in Kuala Lumpur.^[\[70\]](#cite_note-iht-72)^ The so-called [13 May Incident](/wiki/13_May_Incident "13 May Incident") included violent conflicts between members of the [Malay](/wiki/Malaysian_Malays "Malaysian Malays") and the [Chinese](/wiki/Malaysian_Chinese "Malaysian Chinese") communities, the result of Malays' dissatisfaction with their socio-political status. The riots caused the deaths of 196 people, according to official figures,^[\[70\]](#cite_note-iht-72)^ and led to major changes in the country's economic policy to promote and prioritise Malay economic development over that of other ethnicities.{#cite_ref-iht_72-1}  

#### City, Federal Territory, Greater Kuala Lumpur {#City.2C_Federal_Territory.2C_Greater_Kuala_Lumpur}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: City, Federal Territory, Greater Kuala Lumpur")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Kuala_Lumpur_skyline_in_the_1980s.jpg/220px-Kuala_Lumpur_skyline_in_the_1980s.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur_skyline_in_the_1980s.jpg) Kuala Lumpur cityscape in the 1980s before [KLCC](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Centre "Kuala Lumpur City Centre") was created. The [race track](/wiki/Selangor_Turf_Club "Selangor Turf Club") in the foreground was replaced by the [Petronas Tower](/wiki/Petronas_Tower "Petronas Tower") and [KLCC Park](/wiki/KLCC_Park "KLCC Park") in 1998.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-73)^

Kuala Lumpur achieved [city status](/wiki/Cities_of_Malaysia "Cities of Malaysia") on 1 February 1972,^[\[72\]](#cite_note-:0-74)^^[\[73\]](#cite_note-75)^ becoming the first settlement in Malaysia to be granted the status after independence. Later, on 1 February 1974, Kuala Lumpur became a [federal territory](/wiki/Federal_territories_(Malaysia) "Federal territories (Malaysia)").^[\[74\]](#cite_note-76)^ The territory of Kuala Lumpur expanded to 96 square miles by absorbing the surrounding areas. Kuala Lumpur was ceded by [Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor") to be directly controlled by the [central government](/wiki/Government_of_Malaysia "Government of Malaysia"), and it ceased to be capital of Selangor in 1978 after the city of [Shah Alam](/wiki/Shah_Alam "Shah Alam") was declared the new state capital.^[\[75\]](#cite_note-77)^{#cite_ref-77}

On 14 May 1990, Kuala Lumpur celebrated the centennial of the local council. The new federal territory [Kuala Lumpur flag](/wiki/Flag_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Flag of Kuala Lumpur") and anthem were introduced. [Putrajaya](/wiki/Putrajaya "Putrajaya") was declared a Federal Territory on 1 February 2001, as well as the seat of the federal government.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-78)^ The administrative and judicial functions of the government were shifted from Kuala Lumpur to [Putrajaya](/wiki/Putrajaya "Putrajaya"). Kuala Lumpur however still retained its [legislative function](/wiki/Parliament_of_Malaysia "Parliament of Malaysia"),^[\[77\]](#cite_note-79)^ and remained the home of the [Yang di-Pertuan Agong](/wiki/Yang_di-Pertuan_Agong "Yang di-Pertuan Agong") (Constitutional King).^[\[78\]](#cite_note-80)^{#cite_ref-80}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Klcc_park_5.jpg/220px-Klcc_park_5.jpg)](/wiki/File:Klcc_park_5.jpg) The [Kuala Lumpur City Centre](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Centre "Kuala Lumpur City Centre") (KLCC) in 2020

From the 1990s onwards, major urban developments in the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley") extended the Kuala Lumpur metropolitan area.^[\[79\]](#cite_note-81)^^[\[80\]](#cite_note-82)^ This area, known as [Greater Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Greater_Kuala_Lumpur "Greater Kuala Lumpur"), extends from the Federal Territory of Kuala Lumpur westward to [Port Klang](/wiki/Port_Klang "Port Klang"), east to the edge of the [Titiwangsa Mountains](/wiki/Titiwangsa_Mountains "Titiwangsa Mountains") as well as to the north and south. The area covers other administratively separate towns and cities such as Klang, [Shah Alam](/wiki/Shah_Alam "Shah Alam"), [Putrajaya](/wiki/Putrajaya "Putrajaya") and others,^[\[81\]](#cite_note-83)^^[\[82\]](#cite_note-84)^ and is served by the [Klang Valley Integrated Transit System](/wiki/Klang_Valley_Integrated_Transit_System "Klang Valley Integrated Transit System"). Notable projects undertaken within Kuala Lumpur itself included the development of a new [Kuala Lumpur City Centre](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Centre "Kuala Lumpur City Centre") around [Jalan Ampang](/wiki/Jalan_Ampang "Jalan Ampang") and the [Petronas Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers"), once the world's tallest buildings.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-85)^ The Petronas Towers has since been superseded as the tallest buildings in Kuala Lumpur by [The Exchange 106](/wiki/The_Exchange_106 "The Exchange 106") and [Merdeka 118](/wiki/Merdeka_118 "Merdeka 118"), which is the second tallest building in the world after the [Burj Khalifa](/wiki/Burj_Khalifa "Burj Khalifa") in [Dubai](/wiki/Dubai "Dubai").^[\[84\]](#cite_note-86)^{#cite_ref-86}  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Geography")\]  
Main article: [Geography of Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Geography_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Geography of Kuala Lumpur")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Kuala_Lumpur%2C_Malaysia_Astronaut_Imagery.JPG/220px-Kuala_Lumpur%2C_Malaysia_Astronaut_Imagery.JPG)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur,_Malaysia_Astronaut_Imagery.JPG) A satellite view of Klang Valley or [Greater Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Greater_Kuala_Lumpur "Greater Kuala Lumpur")

The geography of Kuala Lumpur is characterised by the huge [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley"), bordered by the [Titiwangsa Mountains](/wiki/Titiwangsa_Mountains "Titiwangsa Mountains") in the east, several minor ranges in the north and the south, and the [Strait of Malacca](/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca "Strait of Malacca") in the west. Kuala Lumpur is a [Malay](/wiki/Malay_language "Malay language") term that translates to "muddy confluence" and is located at the [confluence](/wiki/Confluence "Confluence") of the [Klang](/wiki/Klang_River "Klang River") and [Gombak](/wiki/Gombak_River "Gombak River") rivers which flow into the Selangor River.^[\[85\]](#cite_note-87)^{#cite_ref-87}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/RAF_RED_ARROWS_RETURN_FROM_GLOBAL_TOUR_PROMOTING_UK_INTERESTS_MOD_45161930.jpg/220px-RAF_RED_ARROWS_RETURN_FROM_GLOBAL_TOUR_PROMOTING_UK_INTERESTS_MOD_45161930.jpg)](/wiki/File:RAF_RED_ARROWS_RETURN_FROM_GLOBAL_TOUR_PROMOTING_UK_INTERESTS_MOD_45161930.jpg) The British [Red Arrows](/wiki/Red_Arrows "Red Arrows") flying over the city in 2016

Located in the centre of Selangor state, Kuala Lumpur was a territory of Selangor State Government. In 1974, Kuala Lumpur was split off from Selangor to form the first [Federal Territory](/wiki/Federal_Territories_(Malaysia) "Federal Territories (Malaysia)") governed directly by the Malaysian federal government. Its location in the most developed state on the west coast of [peninsular Malaysia](/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia "Peninsular Malaysia"), which has a wider stretch of flat land than the east coast, has helped it develop faster than other cities in Malaysia.^[\[86\]](#cite_note-88)^ The municipality covers an area of 243 km^2^ (94 sq mi),^[\[2\]](#cite_note-Laporan_Kiraan_Permulaan_2010-2)^ with an average elevation of 81.95 m (268 ft 10 in) highest point being [Bukit Nanas](/wiki/Bukit_Nanas "Bukit Nanas") at 94 meters above sea level.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-89)^{#cite_ref-89}

{#Weather}  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Climate")\]

|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 Kuala Lumpur                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
|                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 Climate chart ([explanation](/wiki/Template:Climate_chart/How_to_read_a_climate_chart "Template:Climate chart/How to read a climate chart"))                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| |-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------| | J         | F         | M         | A         | M         | J         | J         | A         | S         | O         | N         | D         | | 227 33 24 | 193 33 24 | 270 34 25 | 302 34 25 | 230 34 25 | 146 33 25 | 165 33 24 | 174 33 25 | 220 33 24 | 284 33 24 | 356 32 24 | 281 32 24 | | █ Average max. and min. temperatures in °C                                                                                         |||||||||||| | █ Precipitation totals in mm                                                                                                       ||||||||||||                                                                                                                     |
| |                                                      Imperial conversion                                                      |||||||||||| |-----------|-----------|----------|----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|-----------|----------|----------|----------| | J         | F         | M        | A        | M         | J         | J         | A         | S         | O        | N        | D        | | 8.9 91 75 | 7.6 92 75 | 11 93 76 | 12 93 76 | 9.1 92 77 | 5.7 92 77 | 6.5 91 76 | 6.9 91 76 | 8.7 91 76 | 11 91 76 | 14 90 75 | 11 90 75 | | █ Average max. and min. temperatures in °F                                                                                    |||||||||||| | █ Precipitation totals in inches                                                                                              |||||||||||| |

Protected by the [Titiwangsa Range](/wiki/Titiwangsa_Range "Titiwangsa Range") in the east and Indonesia's [Sumatra](/wiki/Sumatra "Sumatra") Island in the west, Kuala Lumpur is sheltered from strong winds and has a [tropical rainforest climate](/wiki/Tropical_rainforest_climate "Tropical rainforest climate") ([Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") *Af* ), hot, humid and sunny, with abundant rainfall, especially during the [northeast monsoon](/wiki/Monsoon "Monsoon") season from October to March. Temperatures tend to remain constant. Maximums hover between 32 and 35 °C (90 and 95 °F) and sometimes topping 38 °C (100.4 °F), while minimums hover between 23.4 and 24.6 °C (74.1 and 76.3 °F) and have never fallen below 17.8 °C (64.0 °F).^[\[88\]](#cite_note-90)^^[\[89\]](#cite_note-pogodaiklimat-91)^ Kuala Lumpur typically receives at least 2,600 mm (100 in) of rain annually; June to August are relatively dry, but even then rainfall typically exceeds 131 millimetres (5.2 in) a month. Kuala Lumpur is highly prone to severe thunderstorms and lightning strikes. The [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley"), including Kuala Lumpur, is one of the places where thunderstorms are most frequently observed on Earth.{#cite_ref-pogodaiklimat_91-0}

Floods are frequent in Kuala Lumpur after heavy downpours, especially in the city centre, because irrigation structure lags behind the intense development in the city.^[\[90\]](#cite_note-Kuala_Lumpur_Environment-92)^ Smoke from forest fires in nearby [Sumatra](/wiki/Sumatra "Sumatra") and [Kalimantan](/wiki/Kalimantan "Kalimantan") sometimes casts a [haze](/wiki/Haze "Haze") over the region, and is a major source of pollution, along with open burning, motor vehicle emissions, and construction.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-93)^{#cite_ref-93}  
{#cite_ref-WMO_94-0}{#cite_ref-NOAAkualalumpur_96-0}

Governance {#Governance}
------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Governance")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Dewan-Bandaraya-Kuala-Lumpur-01.jpg/150px-Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Dewan-Bandaraya-Kuala-Lumpur-01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Dewan-Bandaraya-Kuala-Lumpur-01.jpg) [Kuala Lumpur City Hall](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Hall "Kuala Lumpur City Hall")

Kuala Lumpur was administered by a [corporation sole](/wiki/Corporation_sole "Corporation sole") called the Federal Capital Commissioner from 1 April 1961, until it was awarded city status in 1972, after which executive power transferred to the [Lord Mayor](/wiki/Lord_Mayor "Lord Mayor") (*Datuk Bandar* ).^[\[96\]](#cite_note-KWP-98)^ 14 mayors have been appointed since then. The current mayor is [Kamarulzaman Mat Salleh](/wiki/Kamarulzaman_Mat_Salleh "Kamarulzaman Mat Salleh"), who has been in office since 17 April 2023.^[\[97\]](#cite_note-99)^{#cite_ref-99}  

### Local government {#Local_government}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Local government")\]

The local administration is carried out by the [Kuala Lumpur City Hall](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Hall "Kuala Lumpur City Hall"), an agency under the [Federal Territories Ministry of Malaysia](/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Federal_Territories_(Malaysia) "Ministry of the Federal Territories (Malaysia)").^[\[96\]](#cite_note-KWP-98)^ It is responsible for public health and sanitation, waste removal and management, town planning, environmental protection and building control, social and economic development, and general maintenance functions of urban infrastructure. Executive power lies with the [mayor](/wiki/Mayor_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Mayor of Kuala Lumpur") in the city hall, who is appointed for three years by the Federal Territories Minister. This system of appointing the mayor has been in place ever since the local government elections were suspended in 1970.^[\[98\]](#cite_note-100)^{#cite_ref-100}  

### Districts {#Districts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Districts")\]

Kuala Lumpur's eleven [parliamentary](/wiki/Dewan_Rakyat "Dewan Rakyat") constituencies, with 2020 population, area, density and percentage of the total are congruent with administrative subdivisions under the authority of the [Kuala Lumpur City Hall](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Hall "Kuala Lumpur City Hall") authority.^[\[99\]](#cite_note-101)^{#cite_ref-101}

### Mukims {#Mukims}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Mukims")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Mukims_of_Kuala_Lumpur.svg/220px-Mukims_of_Kuala_Lumpur.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Mukims_of_Kuala_Lumpur.svg) Mukims of the Federal Territory of Kuala Lumpur

For land administration purposes, the Federal Territory of Kuala Lumpur is divided into eight [mukims](/wiki/Mukim "Mukim"), and several mukim-level *towns* (*pekan* /*bandar*):

### Politics {#Politics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Politics")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Bangunan_Parlimen_Malaysia-01.jpg/285px-Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Bangunan_Parlimen_Malaysia-01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur_Malaysia_Bangunan_Parlimen_Malaysia-01.jpg) The [Malaysia Parliament House](/wiki/Malaysian_Houses_of_Parliament "Malaysian Houses of Parliament") (*Bangunan Parlimen Malaysia* ), located at the end of [Jalan Parlimen](/wiki/Jalan_Parlimen "Jalan Parlimen").  
Further information: [Politics of Malaysia](/wiki/Politics_of_Malaysia "Politics of Malaysia")

| [Members of Parliament for Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Members_of_the_Dewan_Rakyat,_15th_Malaysian_Parliament#Federal_Territory_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Members of the Dewan Rakyat, 15th Malaysian Parliament") [Malaysian general election, 2022](/wiki/Malaysian_general_election,_2022 "Malaysian general election, 2022") [![Map](https://maps.wikimedia.org/img/osm-intl,11,3.141,101.6757,250x300.png?lang=en&domain=en.wikipedia.org&title=Kuala_Lumpur&revid=1275141873&groups=_d29addc91c1438b8ef2780d255a1690839d1636f)](/wiki/Special:Map/11/3.141/101.6757/en) Map ||
| [DAP (PH)](/wiki/Democratic_Action_Party_(Malaysia) "Democratic Action Party (Malaysia)") | 5 / 11 |
| [PKR (PH)](/wiki/People%27s_Justice_Party_(Malaysia) "People's Justice Party (Malaysia)") | 5 / 11 |
|                              [UMNO (BN)](/wiki/UMNO "UMNO")                               | 1 / 11 |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|--------|

Kuala Lumpur is home to the [Parliament of Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysian_Houses_of_Parliament "Malaysian Houses of Parliament"). The federal Constitution stipulates the three branches of the Malaysian government: the Executive, Judiciary and Legislative branches. The Parliament consists of the [Dewan Negara](/wiki/Dewan_Negara "Dewan Negara") (Upper House / House of Senate) and [Dewan Rakyat](/wiki/Dewan_Rakyat "Dewan Rakyat") (Lower House / House of Representatives).^[\[10\]](#cite_note-Ibrahim,_2007-12)^{#cite_ref-Ibrahim,_2007_12-1}

While [DBKL](/wiki/Dewan_Bandaraya_Kuala_Lumpur "Dewan Bandaraya Kuala Lumpur") acts as the sole local government in Kuala Lumpur.  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Economy")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/KL-CentralMarket_pedmall.JPG/170px-KL-CentralMarket_pedmall.JPG)](/wiki/File:KL-CentralMarket_pedmall.JPG) A pedestrian mall by the [Central Market](/wiki/Central_Market,_Kuala_Lumpur "Central Market, Kuala Lumpur")

Kuala Lumpur and its surrounding urban areas form the most industrialised and economically, the fastest-growing region in Malaysia.^[\[100\]](#cite_note-metro-102)^ Despite the relocation of federal government administration to [Putrajaya](/wiki/Putrajaya "Putrajaya"), certain government institutions such as [Bank Negara Malaysia](/wiki/Bank_Negara_Malaysia "Bank Negara Malaysia") (*National Bank of Malaysia* ), Companies Commission of Malaysia and Securities Commission as well as most embassies and diplomatic missions have remained in the city.^[\[101\]](#cite_note-103)^ The city remains the economic and business hub of the country. Kuala Lumpur is a centre for finance, insurance, real estate, media and the arts of Malaysia. Kuala Lumpur is rated the only [global city](/wiki/Global_city "Global city") in Malaysia, according to the Globalization and World Cities Study Group and Network (GaWC).^[\[102\]](#cite_note-104)^{#cite_ref-104}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Merdeka_118_View_from_Kuala_Lumpur_Tower_2023.jpg/170px-Merdeka_118_View_from_Kuala_Lumpur_Tower_2023.jpg)](/wiki/File:Merdeka_118_View_from_Kuala_Lumpur_Tower_2023.jpg) The [Merdeka 118](/wiki/Merdeka_118 "Merdeka 118") is the tallest building in Southeast Asia; it is also the second-tallest building in the world, after the [Burj Khalifa](/wiki/Burj_Khalifa "Burj Khalifa").

[Bursa Malaysia](/wiki/Bursa_Malaysia "Bursa Malaysia"), or the Malaysia Exchange, is based in the city and forms one of its core economic activities. As of 5 July 2013, the market capitalisation stood at US$505.67 billion.^[\[103\]](#cite_note-105)^ The [gross domestic product](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") (GDP) for Kuala Lumpur is estimated at RM73,536 million in 2008 with an average annual growth rate of 5.9 per cent.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-DSM-106)^^[\[105\]](#cite_note-107)^ By 2015, the GDP had reached RM160,388 million, representing 15.1% of the total GDP of Malaysia.^[\[106\]](#cite_note-gdp_by_state-108)^ The per capita GDP for Kuala Lumpur in 2013 was RM79,752 with an average annual growth rate of 5.6 per cent,^[\[107\]](#cite_note-109)^ and RM94,722 in 2015.^[\[106\]](#cite_note-gdp_by_state-108)^ Average monthly household income is RM9,073 (\~$2,200) as of 2016, growing at a pace of approximately 6% a year.^[\[108\]](#cite_note-110)^ The service sector, comprising finance, insurance, real estate, business services, wholesale and retail trade, restaurants and hotels, transport, storage and communication, utilities, personal services and government services form the largest component of employment, representing about 83.0 per cent of the total.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^ The remaining 17 per cent comes from manufacturing and construction.{#cite_ref-KEB_111-0}

The large service sector is evident in the number of local and foreign banks and insurance companies operating in the city. Kuala Lumpur is poised to become the global Islamic financing hub^[\[110\]](#cite_note-112)^ with an increasing number of financial institutions providing Islamic financing and the strong presence of Gulf financial institutions such as the world's largest Islamic bank, the [Al-Rajhi Bank](/wiki/Al-Rajhi_Bank "Al-Rajhi Bank")^[\[111\]](#cite_note-113)^ and [Kuwait Finance House](/wiki/Kuwait_Finance_House "Kuwait Finance House"). Apart from that, the [Dow Jones \& Company](/wiki/Dow_Jones_%26_Company "Dow Jones & Company") is keen to work with Bursa Malaysia to set up Islamic Exchange Trade Funds (ETFs), which would help raise Malaysia's profile in the Gulf.^[\[112\]](#cite_note-114)^ The city has a large number of foreign corporations and is also host to many multi national companies' regional offices or support centres, particularly for finance and accounting, and information technology functions. Most of the country's largest companies have their headquarters here, and as of December 2007 and excluding [Petronas](/wiki/Petronas "Petronas"), there are 14 companies that are listed in [Forbes 2000](/wiki/Forbes_2000 "Forbes 2000") based in Kuala Lumpur.^[\[113\]](#cite_note-115)^{#cite_ref-115}

There has been growing emphasis on expanding the economic scope of the city in other service activities, such as research and development, which support the rest of the economy of Malaysia. Kuala Lumpur has been home for years to important research centres such as the [Rubber Research Institute of Malaysia](/wiki/Rubber_Research_Institute_of_Malaysia "Rubber Research Institute of Malaysia"), the [Forest Research Institute Malaysia](/wiki/Forest_Research_Institute_Malaysia "Forest Research Institute Malaysia") and the Institute of Medical Research.^[\[114\]](#cite_note-116)^ A new [financial district](/wiki/Financial_district "Financial district") for Kuala Lumpur is currently under construction: the [Tun Razak Exchange (TRX)](/wiki/Tun_Razak_Exchange "Tun Razak Exchange"), formerly known as Kuala Lumpur International Financial District (KLIFD). The TRX's landmark and prominent building is [The Exchange 106](/wiki/The_Exchange_106 "The Exchange 106") tower. The 70-acre development will be situated in the heart of Kuala Lumpur and will serve international finance and business opportunities. The new financial hub is a strategic enabler of the Malaysian government's [Economic Transformation Programme (ETP)](/wiki/Economic_Transformation_Programme "Economic Transformation Programme"), an initiative by the [Malaysian government](/wiki/Malaysian_Government "Malaysian Government") to turn Malaysia into a [high income economy](/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy") nation.{#cite_ref-116}  

### Tourism {#Tourism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Tourism")\]  
Further information: [Tourism in Malaysia](/wiki/Tourism_in_Malaysia "Tourism in Malaysia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kuala_Lumpur._The_Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building._Central_part._2019-12-01_23-33-18.jpg/220px-Kuala_Lumpur._The_Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building._Central_part._2019-12-01_23-33-18.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur._The_Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building._Central_part._2019-12-01_23-33-18.jpg) [Sultan Abdul Samad Building](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building "Sultan Abdul Samad Building"), a historic building designed in the Moorish style and formerly housed various government offices.

[Tourism](/wiki/Tourism "Tourism") plays an important role in the city's [service-driven](/wiki/Service_sector "Service sector") economy. Many large worldwide [hotel chains](/wiki/Hotel_chain "Hotel chain") have a presence in the city. One of the oldest hotels is the [Hotel Majestic](/wiki/Hotel_Majestic_(Kuala_Lumpur) "Hotel Majestic (Kuala Lumpur)"). Kuala Lumpur is the [sixth most visited city in the world](/wiki/List_of_cities_by_international_visitors "List of cities by international visitors"), with 8.9 million tourists per year.^[\[115\]](#cite_note-117)^^[\[116\]](#cite_note-118)^ Tourism here is driven by the city's cultural diversity, relatively low costs, and wide [gastronomic](/wiki/Gastronomic "Gastronomic") and shopping variety. [MICE](/wiki/Meetings,_incentives,_conferencing,_exhibitions "Meetings, incentives, conferencing, exhibitions") tourism, which mainly encompasses [conventions](/wiki/Convention_(meeting) "Convention (meeting)")--- has expanded in recent years to become a vital component of the industry, and is expected to grow further once the Malaysian government's [Economic Transformation Programme](/wiki/Economic_Transformation_Programme "Economic Transformation Programme") kicks in, and with the completion of a new 93,000 square meter-size [MATRADE Centre](/wiki/MATRADE_Exhibition_and_Convention_Centre "MATRADE Exhibition and Convention Centre") in 2014.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-119)^ The [MATRADE](/wiki/Malaysia_External_Trade_Development_Corporation "Malaysia External Trade Development Corporation") agency is also the owner of the [Malaysia International Trade And Exhibition Centre](/wiki/Malaysia_International_Trade_and_Exhibition_Centre "Malaysia International Trade and Exhibition Centre") (MITEC), the largest trade and exhibition centre of [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia"), which is a component of the larger [KL Metropolis](/wiki/KL_Metropolis "KL Metropolis") development situated in the suburb of [Segambut](/wiki/Segambut "Segambut"). Another notable trend is the increased presence of [budget hotels](/wiki/Budget_hotel "Budget hotel") in the city.{#cite_ref-119}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Muzium_Negara_Malaysia_KL_%282022-05%29.jpg/220px-Muzium_Negara_Malaysia_KL_%282022-05%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Muzium_Negara_Malaysia_KL_(2022-05).jpg) The [National Museum of Malaysia](/wiki/National_Museum_(Malaysia) "National Museum (Malaysia)"), located along Jalan Damansara.

The major tourist destinations in Kuala Lumpur include the [Petronas Twin Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers"), the [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang") shopping district, the [Kuala Lumpur Tower](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Tower "Kuala Lumpur Tower"), [Petaling Street](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street") (Chinatown), the [Merdeka Square](/wiki/Merdeka_Square,_Kuala_Lumpur "Merdeka Square, Kuala Lumpur"), the [Kuala Lumpur railway station](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_railway_station "Kuala Lumpur railway station"), the [House of Parliament](/wiki/Malaysian_Houses_of_Parliament "Malaysian Houses of Parliament") building, the [National Palace](/wiki/Istana_Negara,_Jalan_Duta "Istana Negara, Jalan Duta") (*Istana Negara* ), the [National Planetarium](/wiki/Planetarium_Negara "Planetarium Negara"), the [National Science Centre](/wiki/Pusat_Sains_Negara "Pusat Sains Negara"), the [National Art Gallery](/wiki/National_Visual_Arts_Gallery_(Malaysia) "National Visual Arts Gallery (Malaysia)") (*Balai Seni Negara* ), the [National Theatre](/wiki/Istana_Budaya "Istana Budaya") (*Istana Budaya* ), the [National Museum](/wiki/National_Museum_(Malaysia) "National Museum (Malaysia)"), the [Royal Museum](/wiki/Istana_Negara,_Jalan_Istana "Istana Negara, Jalan Istana"), the [National Textile Museum](/wiki/National_Textile_Museum "National Textile Museum"), [Islamic Arts Museum](/wiki/Islamic_Arts_Museum_Malaysia "Islamic Arts Museum Malaysia"), [Telekom Museum](/wiki/Telekom_Museum "Telekom Museum"), [Royal Malaysian Police Museum](/wiki/Royal_Malaysian_Police_Museum "Royal Malaysian Police Museum"), the [National Mosque of Malaysia](/wiki/National_Mosque_of_Malaysia "National Mosque of Malaysia") (*Masjid Negara* ), [Federal Territory Mosque](/wiki/Federal_Territory_Mosque "Federal Territory Mosque") (*Masjid Wilayah* ), [Sultan Abdul Samad Building](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Building "Sultan Abdul Samad Building"), [DBKL City Theatre](/wiki/Panggung_Bandaraya_DBKL "Panggung Bandaraya DBKL") (*Panggung Bandaraya* ), [Medan Pasar](/wiki/Medan_Pasar "Medan Pasar"), [Central Market](/wiki/Central_Market,_Kuala_Lumpur "Central Market, Kuala Lumpur"), [KL Bird Park](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Bird_Park "Kuala Lumpur Bird Park"), [KL Butterfly Park](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Butterfly_Park "Kuala Lumpur Butterfly Park"), [Aquaria KLCC](/wiki/Aquaria_KLCC "Aquaria KLCC"), [Saloma Link](/wiki/Saloma_Link "Saloma Link") (*Pintasan Saloma* ), the [National Monument](/wiki/National_Monument_(Malaysia) "National Monument (Malaysia)"), and religious sites such as the [Sultan Abdul Samad Jamek Mosque](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Samad_Jamek_Mosque "Sultan Abdul Samad Jamek Mosque"), [Thean Hou Temple](/wiki/Thean_Hou_Temple "Thean Hou Temple") and [Buddhist Maha Vihara](/wiki/Buddhist_Maha_Vihara,_Brickfields "Buddhist Maha Vihara, Brickfields") in [Brickfields](/wiki/Brickfields,_Kuala_Lumpur "Brickfields, Kuala Lumpur").^[\[118\]](#cite_note-120)^^[\[119\]](#cite_note-121)^{#cite_ref-121}

Kuala Lumpur plays host to many cultural festivals such as the [Thaipusam](/wiki/Thaipusam "Thaipusam") procession at the [Sri Mahamariamman Temple](/wiki/Sri_Mahamariamman_Temple,_Kuala_Lumpur "Sri Mahamariamman Temple, Kuala Lumpur"). Every year during the Thaipusam celebration, a silver chariot carrying the statue of [Lord Muruga](/wiki/Kartikeya "Kartikeya") together with his consort [Valli](/wiki/Valli "Valli") and Teivayanni would be paraded through the city beginning at the temple all the way to [Batu Caves](/wiki/Batu_Caves "Batu Caves") in the neighbouring [Gombak](/wiki/Gombak_District "Gombak District"), Selangor.^[\[120\]](#cite_note-122)^ The primary entertainment and shopping district of the city is mainly centred in the Golden Triangle encompassing*[Jalan P. Ramlee](/wiki/Jalan_P._Ramlee "Jalan P. Ramlee")* , *[Jalan Sultan Ismail](/wiki/Jalan_Sultan_Ismail "Jalan Sultan Ismail")* , *[Jalan Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Jalan_Bukit_Bintang "Jalan Bukit Bintang")* , [Ampang Road](/wiki/Jalan_Ampang "Jalan Ampang") and [Bintang Walk](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang").^[\[121\]](#cite_note-123)^{#cite_ref-123}  

### Retail {#Retail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Retail")\]  
Further information: [Shopping in Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Shopping_in_Kuala_Lumpur "Shopping in Kuala Lumpur") and [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang")

Kuala Lumpur alone has 66 shopping malls and is the retail and fashion hub of both Malaysia and [Southeast Asia](/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia").^[\[122\]](#cite_note-124)^ Shopping in Malaysia contributed RM7.7 billion (US$2.26 billion) or 20.8 per cent of the RM31.9 billion tourism receipts in 2006.^[\[123\]](#cite_note-125)^{#cite_ref-125}

[Suria KLCC](/wiki/Suria_KLCC "Suria KLCC") is one of Malaysia's premier upscale shopping destinations due to its location beneath the [Petronas Twin Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Twin_Towers "Petronas Twin Towers"). Apart from [Suria KLCC](/wiki/Suria_KLCC "Suria KLCC"), the [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang") district has the highest concentration of shopping malls in Kuala Lumpur. It includes: [Pavilion KL](/wiki/Pavilion_Kuala_Lumpur "Pavilion Kuala Lumpur"), [Fahrenheit 88](/wiki/Fahrenheit_88 "Fahrenheit 88"), [Plaza Low Yat](/wiki/Plaza_Low_Yat "Plaza Low Yat"), [Berjaya Times Square](/wiki/Berjaya_Times_Square "Berjaya Times Square"), [Lot 10](/wiki/Lot_10 "Lot 10"), [Sungei Wang Plaza](/wiki/Sungei_Wang_Plaza "Sungei Wang Plaza"), [Starhill Gallery](/wiki/Starhill_Gallery "Starhill Gallery"), [Lalaport BBCC](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang_City_Centre "Bukit Bintang City Centre"), [Quill City Mall](/wiki/Quill_City "Quill City") and Avenue K.^[\[124\]](#cite_note-126)^ Changkat area of [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang") hosts various cafes, [alfresco](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/alfresco "wikt:alfresco") dining outlets, illegal activities such as prostitution and more. It is best known as one of the [red-light districts](/wiki/List_of_red-light_districts "List of red-light districts") in Kuala Lumpur. [Bangsar](/wiki/Bangsar "Bangsar") district also has a few shopping complexes, including Bangsar Village, Bangsar Shopping Centre, KL Gateway Mall, [Bangsar South](/wiki/Bangsar_South "Bangsar South"), [KL Eco City Mall](/wiki/KL_Eco_City "KL Eco City"), The Gardens, and [Mid Valley Megamall](/wiki/Mid_Valley_Megamall "Mid Valley Megamall").{#cite_ref-126}

Apart from shopping complexes, Kuala Lumpur has designated numerous zones in the city to market locally manufactured products such as [textiles](/wiki/Textile "Textile"), [fabrics](/wiki/Fabric "Fabric") and [handicrafts](/wiki/Handicraft "Handicraft") especially at [Jalan Tuanku Abdul Rahman](/wiki/Jalan_Tuanku_Abdul_Rahman "Jalan Tuanku Abdul Rahman"). Traditional clothing of ethnic Malays such as [baju Kurung](/wiki/Baju_Kurung "Baju Kurung") and [baju kebaya](/wiki/Kebaya "Kebaya") can be found here. The Chinatown of Kuala Lumpur, commonly known as [Petaling Street](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street"), is one of them. Chinatown features many pre-independence buildings with [Straits Chinese](/wiki/Straits_Chinese "Straits Chinese") and colonial architectural influences.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-gurstien-127)^^[\[126\]](#cite_note-gurstien_google_cache-128)^{#cite_ref-gurstien_google_cache_128-0}

Since 2000, the [Malaysian Ministry of Tourism](/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism,_Arts_and_Culture "Ministry of Tourism, Arts and Culture") introduced a mega sale event for shopping in Malaysia. The mega sale event is held three times a year -- in March, May and December -- in which all shopping malls are encouraged to participate to boost Kuala Lumpur as a leading shopping destination in [Asia](/wiki/Asia "Asia") which has been maintained until present with new mega sales.^[\[127\]](#cite_note-129)^{#cite_ref-129}
