  [Pasar Seni](/wiki/Central_Market,_Kuala_Lumpur "Central Market, Kuala Lumpur") (Central Market), known for its art and craft souvenirs based on [Malaysian culture](/wiki/Culture_of_Malaysia "Culture of Malaysia").
  * [![The Carigali Tower, Petronas Twin Towers, Maxis Tower and Four Seasons Place KL from left.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Twins_SE_Asia_2019_%2849171985716%29.jpg/293px-The_Twins_SE_Asia_2019_%2849171985716%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Twins_SE_Asia_2019_(49171985716).jpg "The Carigali Tower, Petronas Twin Towers, Maxis Tower and Four Seasons Place KL from left.")  
  The [Carigali Tower](/wiki/Petronas_Tower_3 "Petronas Tower 3"), [Petronas Twin Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers"), [Maxis Tower](/wiki/Maxis_Tower "Maxis Tower") and [Four Seasons Place KL](/wiki/Four_Seasons_Place_Kuala_Lumpur "Four Seasons Place Kuala Lumpur") from left.
  * [![Four of the tallest structures in Kuala Lumpur in a single panorama, April 2024.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/KL_city_skyline_April_2024.jpg/413px-KL_city_skyline_April_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:KL_city_skyline_April_2024.jpg "Four of the tallest structures in Kuala Lumpur in a single panorama, April 2024.")  
  Four of the tallest structures in Kuala Lumpur in a single panorama, April 2024.

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Demographics")\]  
{#cite_ref-2020_population_130-0}

| Ethnicities of Kuala Lumpur -- 2020 Census^[\[128\]](#cite_note-2020_population-130)^ |||||
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Ethnic group ||   | Percent ||
| Bumiputras ||   | 47.7% ||
| [Chinese](/wiki/Malaysian_Chinese "Malaysian Chinese") ||   | 41.6% ||
| [Indians](/wiki/Malaysian_Indian "Malaysian Indian") ||   | 10.0% ||
| Others ||   | 0.7% ||
| Population by percentage excluding non-citizens which form 10.5% of KL's population |||||

Kuala Lumpur is the most populous city in Malaysia, with a population of 2.076 million in the [city proper](/wiki/City_proper "City proper") as of 2024^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit)^. It has a population density of 8,157 inhabitants per square kilometre (21,130/sq mi), and is the most densely populated administrative district in Malaysia.^[\[2\]](#cite_note-Laporan_Kiraan_Permulaan_2010-2)^ Residents of the city are colloquially known as [KLites](/wiki/KLites "KLites").^[\[129\]](#cite_note-131)^ Kuala Lumpur is also the centre of the wider [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley") metropolitan area covering [Petaling Jaya](/wiki/Petaling_Jaya "Petaling Jaya"), [Klang](/wiki/Klang_(city) "Klang (city)"), [Subang Jaya](/wiki/Subang_Jaya "Subang Jaya"), [Puchong](/wiki/Puchong "Puchong"), [Shah Alam](/wiki/Shah_Alam "Shah Alam"), and [Gombak](/wiki/Gombak "Gombak"), with an estimated metropolitan population of 7.25 million as of 2017^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit)^.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-131}

Kuala Lumpur's heterogeneous populace includes the country's three major ethnic groups: the [Malays](/wiki/Malaysian_Malays "Malaysian Malays"), the [Chinese](/wiki/Malaysian_Chinese "Malaysian Chinese"), and the [Indians](/wiki/Malaysian_Indian "Malaysian Indian"), although the city also has a mix of different cultures including Eurasians, [Kadazans](/wiki/Kadazan "Kadazan"), [Ibans](/wiki/Iban_people "Iban people") and other Indigenous races from around Malaysia.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^^[\[130\]](#cite_note-AWD-132)^{#cite_ref-AWD_132-0}  

### Historical demographics {#Historical_demographics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Historical demographics")\]
{#cite_ref-ooi_32-4}

| Year |           |         |
| 1890 |  20,000   |   ---   |
| 1900 |  30,000   | +50.0%  |
| 1931 |  111,418  | +271.4% |
| 1957 |  316,537  | +184.1% |
| 1970 |  451,201  | +42.5%  |
| 1974 |  612,004  | +35.6%  |
| 1980 |  919,610  | +50.3%  |
| 1991 | 1,145,342 | +24.5%  |
| 2000 | 1,305,792 | +14.0%  |
| 2010 | 1,588,750 | +21.7%  |
| 2020 | 1,982,112 | +24.8%  |
|------|-----------|---------|
| |----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------| | ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1d/Information_icon4.svg/40px-Information_icon4.svg.png) | Graphs are unavailable due to technical issues. Updates on reimplementing the Graph extension, which will be known as the Chart extension, can be found on [Phabricator](https://phabricator.wikimedia.org/tag/charts/) and on [MediaWiki.org](https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Extension:Chart "mw:Extension:Chart"). | |||
| Kuala Lumpur expanded as a Federal Territory in 1974 Source: ^[\[131\]](#cite_note-2020KF-133)^^[\[132\]](#cite_note-shirley-134)^^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^ |||
[Historical population]

Historically Kuala Lumpur was a predominantly Chinese city, although more recently the [Bumiputera](/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia) "Bumiputera (Malaysia)") component of the city has grown substantially and they are now the dominant group. The Kuala Lumpur of 1872 beside the Klang River was described by Frank Swettenham as a "purely Chinese village", although a Malay [stockade](/wiki/Stockade "Stockade") already existed at [Bukit Nanas](/wiki/Bukit_Nanas "Bukit Nanas") at that time.^[\[28\]](#cite_note-gulllick_3-30)^ By 1875, after participation in the [Selangor Civil War](/wiki/Selangor_Civil_War "Selangor Civil War") by Pahang Malays had ended, Swettenham noted Malay quarters near the Chinese area in a sketch map he had drawn. There were said to be 1,000 Chinese and 700 Malays in the town in this period. Many of the Malays may have settled in Kuala Lumpur after the war.^[\[28\]](#cite_note-gulllick_3-30)^ The population of Kuala Lumpur had increased to around three thousand in 1880 when it was made the capital of Selangor.^[\[133\]](#cite_note-population-135)^ A significant component of the Malay population in Kuala Lumpur of this period consisted of Malays recruited by the British in 1880, mostly from rural [Malacca](/wiki/Malacca "Malacca"), to establish a police force of 2--300, many of whom brought their families.^[\[134\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGullick200043-136)^ Many of the Malays were originally from the other islands of [Malay Archipelago](/wiki/Malay_Archipelago "Malay Archipelago") i.e. Sumatra and Java. The [Mandailings](/wiki/Mandailing_people "Mandailing people"), the [Minangkabaus](/wiki/Minangkabau_people "Minangkabau people"), [Javanese](/wiki/Javanese_people "Javanese people"), and [Buginese](/wiki/Bugis_people "Bugis people") began arriving in Kuala Lumpur in the 19th century, while the [Acehnese](/wiki/Acehnese_people "Acehnese people") arrived in the late 20th century.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-137)^ In the following decades that saw the rebuilding of the town, it grew considerably with a large influx of immigrants, due in large part to the construction of a railway line in 1886 connecting Kuala Lumpur and [Klang](/wiki/Klang_(city) "Klang (city)").^[\[30\]](#cite_note-ooi-32)^{#cite_ref-ooi_32-5}

A census in 1891 of uncertain accuracy gave a figure of 43,796 inhabitants, 79% of whom were Chinese (71% of the Chinese were [Hakka](/wiki/Hakka_people "Hakka people"), but possibly over-counted), 14% Malay, and 6% Indian.^[\[133\]](#cite_note-population-135)^ Another perhaps more accurate survey put the population of Kuala Lumpur in 1891 at around 19,000, with 73% Chinese and 12% each for both Malays and Indians.^[\[136\]](#cite_note-138)^ The rubber boom in the early 20th century led to a further increase in population, from 30,000 in 1900 to 80,000 in 1920.^[\[61\]](#cite_note-gullick_3-63)^ In 1931, 61% of Kuala Lumpur's 111,418 inhabitants were Chinese,^[\[132\]](#cite_note-shirley-134)^ and in 1947 63.5%. The Malays however began to settle in Kuala Lumpur in significant numbers, in part due to government employment, as well as the expansion of the city that absorbed the surrounding rural areas where many Malays lived. Between 1947 and 1957 the population of Malays in Kuala Lumpur increased from 12.5 to 15%, while the proportion of Chinese dropped.^[\[137\]](#cite_note-139)^ The process continued after Malayan independence with the growth of a largely Malay civil service, and later the implementation of the [New Economic Policy](/wiki/Malaysian_New_Economic_Policy "Malaysian New Economic Policy") which encouraged Malay participation in urban industries and business. In 1980 the population of Kuala Lumpur had reached over a million,^[\[57\]](#cite_note-reassessment-59)^ with 52% Chinese, 33% Malay, and 15% Indian.^[\[138\]](#cite_note-140)^ From 1980 to 2000 the number of Bumiputeras increased by 77%, but the Chinese still outnumbered the Bumiputeras in Kuala Lumpur in the 2000 census at 43% compared to 38%.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^^[\[72\]](#cite_note-:0-74)^ By the 2010 census, according to the Department of Statistics and excluding non-citizens, the Malay population in Kuala Lumpur had increased to 44.7% (45.9% [Bumiputera](/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia) "Bumiputera (Malaysia)")), exceeding the Chinese population of 43.2%.^[\[139\]](#cite_note-Department_of_Statistics,_Malaysia-141)^ In the 2020 census, the percentage of the [Bumiputera](/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia) "Bumiputera (Malaysia)") population in Kuala Lumpur had reached around 47.7%, with the Chinese population at 41.6% and Indians 10.0%.^[\[128\]](#cite_note-2020_population-130)^{#cite_ref-2020_population_130-1}

A notable phenomenon in recent times has been the increased portion of foreign residents in Kuala Lumpur, which rose from 1% of the city's population in 1980 to about 8% in the 2000 census, 9.4% in 2010, and 10.5% in the 2020 census.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^^[\[139\]](#cite_note-Department_of_Statistics,_Malaysia-141)^^[\[128\]](#cite_note-2020_population-130)^ These figures also do not include a significant number of [illegal immigrants](/wiki/Illegal_immigrants_in_Malaysia "Illegal immigrants in Malaysia").^[\[140\]](#cite_note-142)^ Kuala Lumpur's rapid development has triggered a huge influx of low-skilled [foreign workers](/wiki/Foreign_worker "Foreign worker") from [Indonesia](/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia"), [Nepal](/wiki/Nepal "Nepal"), [Myanmar](/wiki/Myanmar "Myanmar"), [Thailand](/wiki/Thailand "Thailand"), [Bangladesh](/wiki/Bangladesh "Bangladesh"), [India](/wiki/India "India"), [Pakistan](/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan"), [Sri Lanka](/wiki/Sri_Lanka "Sri Lanka"), [Philippines](/wiki/Philippines "Philippines"), [Vietnam](/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam"), [Laos](/wiki/Laos "Laos") and [Cambodia](/wiki/Cambodia "Cambodia") into Malaysia, many of whom enter the country illegally or without proper permits.^[\[141\]](#cite_note-PDO-143)^^[\[142\]](#cite_note-144)^{#cite_ref-144}

Birth rates in Kuala Lumpur have declined and resulted in a lower proportion of young people -- the proportion of those below 15 years old fell from 33% in 1980 to slightly less than 27% in 2000.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^ On the other hand, the working age group of 15--59 increased from 63% in 1980 to 67% in 2000.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^ The elderly age group, 60 years old and above has increased from 4% in 1980 and 1991 to 6% in 2000.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-KEB-111)^{#cite_ref-KEB_111-6}  

### Languages and religions {#Languages_and_religions}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Languages and religions")\]  
{#cite_ref-2020_population_130-3}

| Religion in Kuala Lumpur -- 2020 Census^[\[128\]](#cite_note-2020_population-130)^ |||||
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Religion ||   | Percent ||
| [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") ||   | 45.3% ||
| [Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism") ||   | 32.3% ||
| [Hinduism](/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism") ||   | 8.2% ||
| [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") ||   | 6.4% ||
| Others ||   | 1.8% ||
| [No Religion](/wiki/Irreligion "Irreligion") ||   | 6.0% ||

Further information: [Religion in Malaysia](/wiki/Religion_in_Malaysia "Religion in Malaysia") and [Languages of Malaysia](/wiki/Languages_of_Malaysia "Languages of Malaysia")

Kuala Lumpur is pluralistic and religiously diverse. The city has many places of worship catering to the multi-religious population. [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") is practised primarily by the Malays, the Indian Muslim communities, and a small number of Chinese Muslims. [Buddhism](/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism "Mahayana Buddhism"), [Confucianism](/wiki/Confucianism "Confucianism") and [Taoism](/wiki/Taoism "Taoism") are practised mainly among the Chinese. Indians traditionally adhere to Hinduism. Some Chinese and Indians also subscribe to [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity "Christianity").^[\[143\]](#cite_note-145)^ Kuala Lumpur is one of the three states where less than 50% of the population are self-identified Muslims, the other two being [Penang](/wiki/Penang "Penang") and [Sarawak](/wiki/Sarawak "Sarawak"). As of the 2020 Census, the population of Kuala Lumpur was 45.3% [Muslim](/wiki/Muslim "Muslim"), 32.3% [Buddhist](/wiki/Buddhist "Buddhist"), 8.2% [Hindu](/wiki/Hindu "Hindu"), 6.4% [Christian](/wiki/Christians "Christians"), 1.8% of other religions, and 6.0% non-religious.^[\[128\]](#cite_note-2020_population-130)^{#cite_ref-2020_population_130-4}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Places_of_worship_in_KL.png/260px-Places_of_worship_in_KL.png)](/wiki/File:Places_of_worship_in_KL.png) Clockwise from top left: [Masjid Negara](/wiki/Masjid_Negara "Masjid Negara"), [Thean Hou Temple](/wiki/Thean_Hou_Temple "Thean Hou Temple"), [Sri Mahamariamman Temple](/wiki/Sri_Mahamariamman_Temple,_Kuala_Lumpur "Sri Mahamariamman Temple, Kuala Lumpur"), [St. John's Cathedral](/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral_(Kuala_Lumpur) "St. John's Cathedral (Kuala Lumpur)")

Statistics from the 2010 Census indicate that 87.4% of the Chinese population identify as Buddhists, with significant minorities of adherents identifying as Christians (7.9%), [Chinese folk religions](/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion "Chinese folk religion") (2.7%) and Muslims (0.6%). The majority of the Indian population identifies as Hindus (81.1%), with significant minorities of identifying as Christians (7.8%), Muslims (4.9%) and Buddhists (2.1%). The non-Malay *[bumiputera](/wiki/Bumiputera_(Malaysia) "Bumiputera (Malaysia)")* community are predominantly Christians (44.9%), with significant minorities identifying as Muslims (31.2%) and Buddhists (13.5%). All bumiputera Malays are Muslim^[\[144\]](#cite_note-146)^ due to the criterion in the [definition of a Malay in the Malaysian constitution](/wiki/Article_160_of_the_Constitution_of_Malaysia "Article 160 of the Constitution of Malaysia") that they should adhere to Islam.^[\[145\]](#cite_note-147)^{#cite_ref-147}

[Bahasa Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysian_language "Malaysian language") is the principal language in Kuala Lumpur. Majority of local Malays speak Selangor dialect (read as [Johor-Riau](/w/index.php?title=Johor-Riau_(dialect)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Johor-Riau (dialect) (page does not exist)") dialect) but Malays from other parts of the state such as [Kedah](/wiki/Kedah_Malay "Kedah Malay"), [Kelantan](/wiki/Kelantan_Malay "Kelantan Malay") and [Terengganu](/wiki/Terengganu_Malay "Terengganu Malay"), as well as [Sarawak](/wiki/Sarawak_Malay "Sarawak Malay") and also [Brunei Malay](/wiki/Brunei_Malay "Brunei Malay") that was spoken by those from Sabah/Labuan, are significantly using their respective dialect varieties of Malay.

Kuala Lumpur residents are generally literate in English, with a large proportion adopting it as their first language, especially among younger and certain adult generations. [Malaysian English](/wiki/Malaysian_English "Malaysian English") is widely used.^[\[146\]](#cite_note-148)^ It has a strong presence, especially in business, and is taught as a compulsory language in schools.^[\[130\]](#cite_note-AWD-132)^{#cite_ref-AWD_132-1}

In addition, the [Cantonese](/wiki/Malaysian_Cantonese "Malaysian Cantonese") dialect group forms the majority among the local [Chinese](/wiki/Malaysian_Chinese "Malaysian Chinese") population, [Hokkien](/wiki/Penang_Hokkien "Penang Hokkien") and [Mandarin](/wiki/Standard_Mandarin "Standard Mandarin") are prominent, as they are also widely spoken among the Chinese communities.^[\[147\]](#cite_note-149)^ Another major Chinese dialect spoken is [Hakka](/wiki/Hakka_language "Hakka language").{#cite_ref-149}

While [Tamil](/wiki/Malaysian_Tamil "Malaysian Tamil") is dominant among the local [Indian](/wiki/Malaysian_Indian "Malaysian Indian") population, other Indian languages spoken by minorities include [Telugu](/wiki/Telugu_language "Telugu language"), [Malayalam](/wiki/Malayalam "Malayalam"), [Punjabi](/wiki/Punjabi_language "Punjabi language"), and [Hindi](/wiki/Hindi "Hindi").^[\[148\]](#cite_note-150)^{#cite_ref-150}

Besides Malay, there are a variety of languages spoken by people of Indonesian descent, such as [Minangkabau](/wiki/Minangkabau_language "Minangkabau language")^[\[149\]](#cite_note-151)^ and [Javanese](/wiki/Javanese_language "Javanese language").{#cite_ref-151}

There are also various foreign speakers of [Arabic](/wiki/Arabic "Arabic"), [Japanese](/wiki/Japanese_language "Japanese language"), [Korean](/wiki/Korean_language "Korean language"), [Thai](/wiki/Central_Thai_language "Central Thai language"), [Spanish](/wiki/Spanish_language "Spanish language") etc, as well as diverse indigenous languages of [Semai](/wiki/Semai_language "Semai language"), [Iban](/wiki/Iban_language "Iban language"), [Kadazandusun](/wiki/Kadazandusun_language "Kadazandusun language"), [Bidayuh](/wiki/Bidayuh_language "Bidayuh language") and other languages.

----------------------

Panorama view of Kuala Lumpur in 2020  

### Architecture {#Architecture}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Architecture")\]  
Main article: [Architecture of Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Architecture_of_Kuala_Lumpur "Architecture of Kuala Lumpur")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Jalan_Sultan_Hishamuddin_%28Damansara_Road%29_%28south%29%2C_central_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg/220px-Jalan_Sultan_Hishamuddin_%28Damansara_Road%29_%28south%29%2C_central_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg)](/wiki/File:Jalan_Sultan_Hishamuddin_(Damansara_Road)_(south),_central_Kuala_Lumpur.jpg) The [Kuala Lumpur Railway Station](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Railway_Station "Kuala Lumpur Railway Station") (right) contrasts with [Keretapi Tanah Melayu](/wiki/Keretapi_Tanah_Melayu "Keretapi Tanah Melayu") (left) Administration Building, a darker, similarly Mughal-styled building. Both were designed by [A. B. Hubback](/wiki/A._B._Hubback "A. B. Hubback")

The architecture of Kuala Lumpur is a mixture of old [colonial](/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism") influences, Asian traditions, Malay Islamic inspirations, [modern](/wiki/Modern_architecture "Modern architecture"), and [postmodern architecture](/wiki/Postmodern_architecture "Postmodern architecture").^[\[150\]](#cite_note-152)^ A relatively young city compared with other Southeast Asian capitals such as [Bangkok](/wiki/Bangkok "Bangkok"), [Jakarta](/wiki/Jakarta "Jakarta") and [Manila](/wiki/Manila "Manila"), most of Kuala Lumpur's notable colonial-era buildings were built toward the end of the 19th and early 20th centuries. These buildings were designed in a number of styles -- [Mughal](/wiki/Mughal_architecture "Mughal architecture")/[Moorish Revival](/wiki/Moorish_Revival_architecture "Moorish Revival architecture"), [Mock Tudor](/wiki/Mock_Tudor "Mock Tudor"), [Neo-Gothic](/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture "Gothic Revival architecture") or Grecian-Spanish style or architecture.^[\[151\]](#cite_note-153)^ Most of the styling has been modified to use local resources and adapted to the local climate, which is hot and humid all year around. A significant architect of the early period is [Arthur Benison Hubback](/wiki/Arthur_Benison_Hubback "Arthur Benison Hubback") who designed a number of the colonial-era buildings including the [Kuala Lumpur Railway Station](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Railway_Station "Kuala Lumpur Railway Station") and [Jamek Mosque](/wiki/Jamek_Mosque "Jamek Mosque").{#cite_ref-153}

Before the Second World War, many [shophouses](/wiki/Shophouse "Shophouse"), usually two stories with functional shops on the ground floor and separate residential spaces upstairs, were built around the old city centre. These shop-houses drew inspiration from [Straits Chinese](/wiki/Straits_Chinese "Straits Chinese") and European traditions.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-gurstien-127)^^[\[126\]](#cite_note-gurstien_google_cache-128)^ Some of these shophouses have made way for new developments but there are still many standing today in the [Medan Pasar Besar](/wiki/Medan_Pasar_Besar "Medan Pasar Besar") (Old Market Square), [Chinatown](/wiki/Petaling_Street "Petaling Street"), [Jalan Tuanku Abdul Rahman](/wiki/Jalan_Tuanku_Abdul_Rahman "Jalan Tuanku Abdul Rahman"), [Jalan Doraisamy](/wiki/Jalan_Doraisamy "Jalan Doraisamy"), [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang") and Tengkat Tong Shin areas.{#cite_ref-gurstien_google_cache_128-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Masjid_Jamek.jpg/220px-Masjid_Jamek.jpg)](/wiki/File:Masjid_Jamek.jpg) [Jamek Mosque](/wiki/Jamek_Mosque "Jamek Mosque") (*Masjid Jamek* ) is one of the oldest [mosques](/wiki/Mosque "Mosque") still standing in Kuala Lumpur, built in 1909.

Independence coupled with rapid economic growth from the 1970s to the 1990s and with Islam being the official religion in the country, has resulted in the construction of buildings with a more local and Islamic flavour around the city. Many of these buildings derive their design from traditional Malay items such as the [songkok](/wiki/Songkok "Songkok") and the [keris](/wiki/Kris "Kris"). Some of these buildings have Islamic geometric motifs integrated into the designs of the building, due to Islamic restrictions on imitating nature through drawings.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cop149-154)^ Examples of these buildings are [Telekom Tower](/wiki/Telekom_Tower "Telekom Tower"), [Maybank Tower](/wiki/Maybank_Tower_(Kuala_Lumpur) "Maybank Tower (Kuala Lumpur)"), [Dayabumi Complex](/wiki/Dayabumi_Complex "Dayabumi Complex"), and the Islamic Centre.^[\[153\]](#cite_note-155)^ Some buildings such as the Islamic Arts Museum Malaysia and [National Planetarium](/wiki/Planetarium_Negara "Planetarium Negara") have been built to masquerade as a place of worship, complete with [dome](/wiki/Dome "Dome") and [minaret](/wiki/Minaret "Minaret"), when in fact they are places of science and knowledge. The 452-metre (1,483 ft) [Petronas Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers") are the tallest twin buildings in the world and were the tallest buildings in the country until being surpassed by The Exchange 106 by 1.7 meters in 2019.^[\[154\]](#cite_note-156)^ They were designed to resemble motifs found in Islamic art.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-157)^{#cite_ref-157}

Late modern and postmodern architecture began to appear in the late-1990s and early-2000s. With economic development, old buildings such as [Bok House](/wiki/Bok_House "Bok House") have been razed to make way for new ones. Buildings with all-glass shells exist throughout the city, with the most prominent examples being the [Petronas Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers") and [Kuala Lumpur Convention Centre](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Convention_Centre "Kuala Lumpur Convention Centre"). Kuala Lumpur's central business district today has shifted to the Kuala Lumpur city centre (KLCC) where many new and tall buildings with modern and postmodern architecture fill the skyline. According to the World Tallest 50 Urban Agglomeration 2010 Projection by the [Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat](/wiki/Council_on_Tall_Buildings_and_Urban_Habitat "Council on Tall Buildings and Urban Habitat"), Kuala Lumpur ranks 10th among cities that have most buildings above 100 metres with a combined height of 34,035 metres from its 244 high-rise buildings.^[\[156\]](#cite_note-158)^{#cite_ref-158}  

### Parks {#Parks}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Parks")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/2016_Kuala_Lumpur%2C_Park_KLCC%2C_Fontanna_na_jeziorze_Symphony_%2801%29.jpg/220px-2016_Kuala_Lumpur%2C_Park_KLCC%2C_Fontanna_na_jeziorze_Symphony_%2801%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:2016_Kuala_Lumpur,_Park_KLCC,_Fontanna_na_jeziorze_Symphony_(01).jpg) [KLCC Park](/wiki/KLCC_Park "KLCC Park") is a 50-acre urban park located in the city centre.

The [Perdana Botanical Garden](/wiki/Perdana_Botanical_Gardens "Perdana Botanical Gardens") or Lake Gardens, a 92-hectare (230-acre) botanical garden, was the first recreational park created in Kuala Lumpur. The Malaysian Parliament building is located close by, and [Carcosa Seri Negara](/wiki/Carcosa_Seri_Negara "Carcosa Seri Negara"), which was once the official residence of the British colonial administration, is also sited here. The park includes a butterfly park, deer park, orchid garden, a hibiscus garden, and the [Kuala Lumpur Bird Park](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Bird_Park "Kuala Lumpur Bird Park"), which is the world's largest aviary bird park.^[\[157\]](#cite_note-159)^ Other parks in the city include the [ASEAN Sculpture Garden](/wiki/ASEAN_Sculpture_Garden "ASEAN Sculpture Garden"), [KLCC Park](/wiki/KLCC_Park "KLCC Park"), [Titiwangsa Lake Gardens](/wiki/Titiwangsa_Lake_Gardens "Titiwangsa Lake Gardens"), Metropolitan Lake Gardens in [Kepong](/wiki/Kepong "Kepong"), Taman Tasik Permaisuri (Queen's Lake Gardens), [Bukit Kiara](/wiki/Bukit_Kiara "Bukit Kiara") Botanical Gardens, the equestrian park and West Valley Park near [Taman Tun Dr Ismail](/wiki/TTDI "TTDI") (TTDI), and Bukit Jalil International Park.{#cite_ref-159}

There are three forest reserves within the city, the [Bukit Nanas](/wiki/Bukit_Nanas "Bukit Nanas") Forest Reserve in the city centre, the oldest gazetted forest reserve in the country 10.52 ha or 26.0 acres, Bukit Sungai Putih Forest Reserve (7.41 ha or 18.3 acres) and Bukit Sungai Besi Forest Reserve (42.11 ha or 104.1 acres). [Bukit Nanas](/wiki/Bukit_Nanas "Bukit Nanas"), in the heart of the city centre, is one of the oldest virgin forests in the world within a city.^[\[158\]](#cite_note-160)^ These residual forest areas are home to a number of [fauna](/wiki/Fauna "Fauna") species, particularly monkeys, [treeshrews](/wiki/Treeshrew "Treeshrew"), [pygmy goats](/wiki/Pygmy_goat "Pygmy goat"), [budgerigars](/wiki/Budgerigar "Budgerigar"), squirrels and birds.{#cite_ref-160}  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Kuala_Lumpur_-_Titiwangsa_-_Panorama_0002.JPG/1100px-Kuala_Lumpur_-_Titiwangsa_-_Panorama_0002.JPG)](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur_-_Titiwangsa_-_Panorama_0002.JPG "The view of Kuala Lumpur from Titiwangsa Lake Gardens")  
[](/wiki/File:Kuala_Lumpur_-_Titiwangsa_-_Panorama_0002.JPG "File:Kuala Lumpur - Titiwangsa - Panorama 0002.JPG")
The view of Kuala Lumpur from [Titiwangsa Lake Gardens](/wiki/Titiwangsa_Lake_Gardens "Titiwangsa Lake Gardens")  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Education")\]  
See also: [Education in Malaysia](/wiki/Education_in_Malaysia "Education in Malaysia")

According to government statistics, Kuala Lumpur had a [literacy](/wiki/Literacy "Literacy") rate of 97.5% in 2000, the highest rate in any state or territory in Malaysia.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-161)^ In Malaysia, Malay is the language of instruction for most subjects while English is a compulsory subject, but as of 2012^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit)^, English was still the language of instruction for mathematics and the natural sciences for certain schools. Some schools provide instruction in Mandarin and Tamil for certain subjects.^[\[160\]](#cite_note-162)^{#cite_ref-162}

Kuala Lumpur contains 14 tertiary education institutions, 79 high schools, 155 elementary schools, and 136 kindergartens.^[\[161\]](#cite_note-163)^{#cite_ref-163}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/University_of_Malaya_City_View.jpg/220px-University_of_Malaya_City_View.jpg)](/wiki/File:University_of_Malaya_City_View.jpg) [University of Malaya](/wiki/University_of_Malaya "University of Malaya") City View.

Kuala Lumpur is home to the [University of Malaya](/wiki/University_of_Malaya "University of Malaya") (UM). Established in 1949, it is the oldest university in Malaysia, and one of the oldest in the region.^[\[162\]](#cite_note-164)^ It was ranked the best university in Malaysia, the 22nd-best in Asia, and third in [Southeast Asia](/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia") in QS World University Rankings 2019.^[\[163\]](#cite_note-165)^ In recent years, the number of [international students](/wiki/International_students "International students") at the University of Malaya has risen, as a result of increasing efforts made to attract them.^[\[164\]](#cite_note-166)^{#cite_ref-166}

Other universities located in Kuala Lumpur include [Universiti Tunku Abdul Rahman](/wiki/Universiti_Tunku_Abdul_Rahman "Universiti Tunku Abdul Rahman") (UTAR), [University of Malaya-Wales](/wiki/University_of_Malaya-Wales "University of Malaya-Wales") (UM-Wales), [International Islamic University Malaysia](/wiki/International_Islamic_University_Malaysia "International Islamic University Malaysia") (IIUM), [Tunku Abdul Rahman University College](/wiki/Tunku_Abdul_Rahman_University_College "Tunku Abdul Rahman University College") (TARUC), [UCSI University](/wiki/UCSI_University "UCSI University") (UCSI), [Taylor's University](/wiki/Taylor%27s_University "Taylor's University") (TULC), [International Medical University](/wiki/International_Medical_University "International Medical University") (IMU), [Open University Malaysia](/wiki/Open_University_Malaysia "Open University Malaysia") (OUM), [Kuala Lumpur University](/wiki/Universiti_Kuala_Lumpur "Universiti Kuala Lumpur") (UniKL), [Perdana University](/wiki/Perdana_University "Perdana University") (PU), [Wawasan Open University](/wiki/Wawasan_Open_University "Wawasan Open University") (WOU), [HELP University](/wiki/HELP_University "HELP University") and the branch campus of the [National University of Malaysia](/wiki/National_University_of_Malaysia "National University of Malaysia") (UKM) and [University of Technology Malaysia](/wiki/Universiti_Teknologi_Malaysia "Universiti Teknologi Malaysia") (UTM). The [National Defence University of Malaysia](/wiki/Universiti_Pertahanan_Nasional_Malaysia "Universiti Pertahanan Nasional Malaysia") is located at [Sungai Besi](/wiki/Sungai_Besi "Sungai Besi") Army Base, in the southern part of central Kuala Lumpur. It was established to be a major centre for military and defence technology studies. This institution covers studies for the [army](/wiki/Army "Army"), [navy](/wiki/Navy "Navy"), and [air force](/wiki/Air_force "Air force").^[\[165\]](#cite_note-167)^{#cite_ref-167}

Greater Kuala Lumpur covers an even more extensive selection of universities including several international branches such as [Monash University Malaysia Campus](/wiki/Monash_University_Malaysia_Campus "Monash University Malaysia Campus"), [University of Nottingham Malaysia Campus](/wiki/University_of_Nottingham_Malaysia_Campus "University of Nottingham Malaysia Campus") and [Xiamen University Malaysia](/wiki/Xiamen_University_Malaysia "Xiamen University Malaysia").  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Culture")\]  
See also: [Culture of Malaysia](/wiki/Culture_of_Malaysia "Culture of Malaysia")  

### Arts {#Arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Arts")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/KLNationalMuseumFrieze.JPG/220px-KLNationalMuseumFrieze.JPG)](/wiki/File:KLNationalMuseumFrieze.JPG) Frieze depicting Malaysian history at the [National Museum](/wiki/National_Museum_(Malaysia) "National Museum (Malaysia)").

Kuala Lumpur is a hub for cultural activities and events in Malaysia. Among the centres is the [National Museum](/wiki/Muzium_Negara "Muzium Negara"), which is situated along the [Mahameru Highway](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Middle_Ring_Road_1 "Kuala Lumpur Middle Ring Road 1"). Its collection comprises artefacts and paintings collected throughout the country.^[\[166\]](#cite_note-168)^ The [Islamic Arts Museum](/wiki/Islamic_Arts_Museum_Malaysia "Islamic Arts Museum Malaysia"), which houses more than seven thousand Islamic artefacts including rare exhibits and a library of Islamic art books, is the largest Islamic art collection in Southeast Asia.^[\[167\]](#cite_note-169)^ The museum's collection not only concentrates on works from the Middle East but also includes work from elsewhere in Asia, such as China and Southeast Asia. Kuala Lumpur has a craft complex coupled with a museum that displays a variety of textile, ceramic, metal craft, and weaved products. Information on the production process is portrayed in diorama format complete with historical facts, techniques, and traditionally engineered equipment. Among the processes shown are pottery making, intricate wood carving, silver-smithing, weaving [songket](/wiki/Songket "Songket") cloth, stamping [batik](/wiki/Batik "Batik") patterns on cloth, and boat-making.^[\[168\]](#cite_note-170)^{#cite_ref-170}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Saloma_at_Sunset_%2849570270217%29.jpg/220px-Saloma_at_Sunset_%2849570270217%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Saloma_at_Sunset_(49570270217).jpg) The [Saloma Link](/wiki/Saloma_Link "Saloma Link") seen at dusk, with the [Petronas Tower](/wiki/Petronas_Tower "Petronas Tower") behind it.

The premier performing arts venue is the [Petronas Philharmonic Hall](/wiki/Dewan_Filharmonik_Petronas "Dewan Filharmonik Petronas") located underneath the [Petronas Towers](/wiki/Petronas_Towers "Petronas Towers"). The resident orchestra is the [Malaysian Philharmonic Orchestra](/wiki/Malaysian_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Malaysian Philharmonic Orchestra") (MPO), consisting of musicians from all over the world, and features regular concerts, chamber concerts, and traditional cultural performances.^[\[169\]](#cite_note-171)^ The [Kuala Lumpur Performing Arts Centre](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Performing_Arts_Centre "Kuala Lumpur Performing Arts Centre") (KLPac) in Sentul West and Damansara Performing Arts Centre (DPac) in [Damansara Perdana](/wiki/Damansara_Perdana "Damansara Perdana") are two of the most established centres in the country for the performing arts, notably theatre, plays, music, and film screening. It has housed many local productions and has been a supporter of local and regional independent performance artists.^[\[170\]](#cite_note-172)^ The [Future Music Festival Asia](/wiki/Future_Music_Festival_Asia "Future Music Festival Asia") has been held in the city since 2012, featuring local and international artists.^[\[171\]](#cite_note-173)^{#cite_ref-173}

The [National Art Gallery of Malaysia](/wiki/National_Art_Gallery_of_Malaysia "National Art Gallery of Malaysia") is located on Jalan Temerloh, off Jalan Tun Razak on a 5.67-hectare (14.0-acre) site neighbouring the National Theatre ([Istana Budaya](/wiki/Istana_Budaya "Istana Budaya")) and National Library. The architecture of the gallery incorporates elements of traditional Malay architecture, as well as contemporary modern architecture. The National Art Gallery serves as a centre of excellence and is a trustee of the national art heritage. The [Ilham Tower](/wiki/Ilham_Tower "Ilham Tower") Gallery near [Ampang Park](/wiki/Ampang_Park_LRT_station "Ampang Park LRT station") houses exhibitions of works by local and foreign artists.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-174)^{#cite_ref-174}

Kuala Lumpur holds the Malaysia International Gourmet Festival annually.^[\[173\]](#cite_note-175)^ Another event hosted annually by the city is the [Kuala Lumpur Fashion Week](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Fashion_Week "Kuala Lumpur Fashion Week"),^[\[174\]](#cite_note-176)^ which includes international brands and local designers. Also, Kuala Lumpur was designated as the [World Book Capital](/wiki/World_Book_Capital "World Book Capital") for 2020 by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO").^[\[175\]](#cite_note-177)^{#cite_ref-177}  

### Sports and recreation {#Sports_and_recreation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Sports and recreation")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg/220px-National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Stadium_Bukit_Jalil_2014_AFF_Suzuki_Cup_final.jpg) [Bukit Jalil National Stadium](/wiki/Bukit_Jalil_National_Stadium "Bukit Jalil National Stadium") is an all-seater [multi-purpose stadium](/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium "Multi-purpose stadium") that was built in January 1995.

Kuala Lumpur has numerous parks, gardens and open spaces for recreational purposes. Total open space for recreational and sports facilities land use in the city has increased significantly by 169.6 per cent from 5.86 square kilometres (1,450 acres) in 1984 to 15.8 square kilometres (3,900 acres) in 2000.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-Community_Facilities-178)^{#cite_ref-Community_Facilities_178-0}

Kuala Lumpur was touted as one of the host cities for the [Formula One](/wiki/Formula_One "Formula One") World Championship from 1999 to 2017.^[\[177\]](#cite_note-F1-179)^ The open-wheel auto racing [A1 Grand Prix](/wiki/A1_Grand_Prix "A1 Grand Prix")^[\[178\]](#cite_note-180)^ was held until the series folded in 2009. The [Motorcycle Grand Prix](/wiki/Motorcycle_Grand_Prix "Motorcycle Grand Prix")^[\[179\]](#cite_note-181)^ races are held at the [Sepang International Circuit](/wiki/Sepang_International_Circuit "Sepang International Circuit") in [Sepang](/wiki/Sepang "Sepang") in the neighbouring state of [Selangor](/wiki/Selangor "Selangor"). The Formula One event contributed significantly to tourist arrivals and tourism income to Kuala Lumpur. This was evident during the [Asian financial crisis](/wiki/1997_Asian_financial_crisis "1997 Asian financial crisis") in 1998. Despite cities around Asia suffering declining tourist arrivals, in Kuala Lumpur tourist arrivals increased from 6,210,900 in 1997 to 10,221,600 in 2000, or 64.6%.^[\[180\]](#cite_note-Tourism-182)^ In 2015, the [Kuala Lumpur Street Circuit](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Street_Circuit "Kuala Lumpur Street Circuit") was constructed to host the [Kuala Lumpur City Grand Prix](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Grand_Prix "Kuala Lumpur City Grand Prix") motor racing event.{#cite_ref-Tourism_182-0}

[Football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") is one of the most popular sports in Kuala Lumpur. The [Merdeka Tournament](/wiki/Pestabola_Merdeka "Pestabola Merdeka") is mainly held at [Stadium Merdeka](/wiki/Stadium_Merdeka "Stadium Merdeka"). The [Stadium Negara](/wiki/Stadium_Negara "Stadium Negara") is also located right next to it which is also one of the oldest indoor stadiums in the country. The city is also the home of [Kuala Lumpur City](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_F.C. "Kuala Lumpur City F.C."), which plays in the [Malaysia Super League](/wiki/Malaysia_Super_League "Malaysia Super League"). Kuala Lumpur hosted the official [Asian Basketball Championship](/wiki/Asian_Basketball_Championship "Asian Basketball Championship") in [1965](/wiki/1965_ABC_Championship "1965 ABC Championship"), [1977](/wiki/1977_ABC_Championship "1977 ABC Championship") and [1985](/wiki/1985_ABC_Championship "1985 ABC Championship"). The city's basketball supporters cheered [Malaysia's national basketball team](/wiki/Malaysia%27s_national_basketball_team "Malaysia's national basketball team") to a Final Four finish in 1985, the team's best performance to date. Further, the city is home to the [Kuala Lumpur Dragons](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Dragons "Kuala Lumpur Dragons"), 2016 Champions of the [ASEAN Basketball League](/wiki/ASEAN_Basketball_League "ASEAN Basketball League").^[\[181\]](#cite_note-183)^ The team plays its home games in the [MABA Stadium](/wiki/MABA_Stadium "MABA Stadium").{#cite_ref-183}

KL Grand Prix CSI 5\*, a five-star international showjumping equestrian event, is held annually in the city.^[\[182\]](#cite_note-184)^ Other annual sport events hosted by the city include the KL Tower Run,^[\[183\]](#cite_note-185)^ the KL Tower International BASE Jump Merdeka Circuit and the Kuala Lumpur International Marathon. Kuala Lumpur is also one of the stages of the [Tour de Langkawi](/wiki/Tour_de_Langkawi "Tour de Langkawi") cycling race.^[\[184\]](#cite_note-186)^ The annual [Malaysia Open](/wiki/Malaysia_Open_(badminton) "Malaysia Open (badminton)") Super Series badminton tournament is held in Kuala Lumpur.{#cite_ref-186}

Kuala Lumpur is also the birthplace of [Hashing](/wiki/Hash_House_Harriers "Hash House Harriers"), which began in December 1938 when a group of British colonial officers and expatriates, some from the [Selangor Club](/wiki/Selangor_Club "Selangor Club"), began meeting on Monday evenings to run, in a fashion patterned after the traditional British [Paper Chase](/wiki/Paper_Chase_(game) "Paper Chase (game)") or "Hare and Hounds".^[\[185\]](#cite_note-187)^{#cite_ref-187}

Kuala Lumpur hosted the [128th IOC Session](/wiki/128th_IOC_Session "128th IOC Session") in 2015 where the [IOC](/wiki/IOC "IOC") elected [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing") as the host city of the [2022 Winter Olympics](/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics "2022 Winter Olympics")^[\[186\]](#cite_note-188)^ and [Lausanne](/wiki/Lausanne "Lausanne") as the host city of the [2020 Winter Youth Olympics](/wiki/2020_Winter_Youth_Olympics "2020 Winter Youth Olympics").^[\[187\]](#cite_note-189)^{#cite_ref-189}  

Transportation {#Transportation}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
Main articles: [Transportation in Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Transportation_in_Kuala_Lumpur "Transportation in Kuala Lumpur") and [Klang Valley Integrated Transit System](/wiki/Klang_Valley_Integrated_Transit_System "Klang Valley Integrated Transit System")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rukun_Negara_Wall_at_Merdeka_MRT_station.jpg/1000px-Rukun_Negara_Wall_at_Merdeka_MRT_station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Rukun_Negara_Wall_at_Merdeka_MRT_station.jpg "The decorative relief wall portraying the Rukun Negara, the Malaysian national pledge, at the Upper Concourse Level of Merdeka MRT station.")  
[](/wiki/File:Rukun_Negara_Wall_at_Merdeka_MRT_station.jpg "File:Rukun Negara Wall at Merdeka MRT station.jpg")
The decorative relief wall portraying the *[Rukun Negara](/wiki/Rukun_Negara "Rukun Negara")* , the Malaysian national pledge, at the Upper Concourse Level of [Merdeka MRT station](/wiki/Merdeka_MRT_station "Merdeka MRT station").
Road traffic of Jalan Kuching, Kuala Lumpur during noon

As in most other Asian cities, driving is the main commuting choice in Kuala Lumpur.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-prasarana-190)^ Every part of the city is well connected with highways. Kuala Lumpur has a comprehensive [road network](/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Kuala_Lumpur "List of roads in Kuala Lumpur") with more transportation development planned.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-191)^ Public transportation covers a variety of [transport modes](/wiki/Transport_modes "Transport modes") such as [bus](/wiki/Bus "Bus"), [rail](/wiki/Rail_transport "Rail transport") and [taxi](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab"). Despite efforts to promote public transport, utilisation rates are low, 16 per cent of the population in 2006.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-prasarana-190)^ However, public transport utilisation will increase with the expansion of the rail network,^[\[190\]](#cite_note-192)^ operated by [Prasarana Malaysia](/wiki/Prasarana_Malaysia "Prasarana Malaysia") in Kuala Lumpur and the Klang Valley via its subsidiaries [Rapid Rail](/wiki/Rapid_Rail "Rapid Rail") and [Rapid Bus](/wiki/Rapid_Bus "Rapid Bus"), using the [Rapid KL](/wiki/Rapid_KL "Rapid KL") brand name.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-193)^ Since the take over from Intrakota Komposit Sdn Bhd, [Prasarana Malaysia](/wiki/Prasarana_Malaysia "Prasarana Malaysia") has redrawn the entire bus network of Kuala Lumpur and the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley") metropolitan area^[\[192\]](#cite_note-194)^ to increase passenger numbers and improve Kuala Lumpur's public transport system. [Prasarana Malaysia](/wiki/Prasarana_Malaysia "Prasarana Malaysia") has adopted the [hub and spoke](/wiki/Hub_and_spoke "Hub and spoke") system to provide greater connectivity, and reduce the need for more buses.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-195)^^[\[194\]](#cite_note-196)^ [KL Sentral](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Sentral_station "Kuala Lumpur Sentral station") was added on 16 April 2001 and served as the new transport hub of the [Klang Valley Integrated Transit System](/wiki/Klang_Valley_Integrated_Transit_System "Klang Valley Integrated Transit System").{#cite_ref-196}  

### Urban rail {#Urban_rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Urban rail")\]  
Main articles: [Rapid KL](/wiki/Rapid_KL "Rapid KL") and [KTM Komuter](/wiki/KTM_Komuter "KTM Komuter")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/MRT_SBK_Semantan_station2.jpg/98px-MRT_SBK_Semantan_station2.jpg)](/wiki/File:MRT_SBK_Semantan_station2.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Ducky_train_entering_Kampung_Batu_MRT_Station_%28220710%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/90px-Ducky_train_entering_Kampung_Batu_MRT_Station_%28220710%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ducky_train_entering_Kampung_Batu_MRT_Station_(220710)_(cropped).jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/170607_KL_city_centre_from_PWTC.jpg/92px-170607_KL_city_centre_from_PWTC.jpg)](/wiki/File:170607_KL_city_centre_from_PWTC.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/170323_Innovia_Metro_300_at_Lembah_Subang.jpg/137px-170323_Innovia_Metro_300_at_Lembah_Subang.jpg)](/wiki/File:170323_Innovia_Metro_300_at_Lembah_Subang.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/160316_KL_Monorail_leaving_Raja_Chulan_station_%28cropped%29.jpeg/147px-160316_KL_Monorail_leaving_Raja_Chulan_station_%28cropped%29.jpeg)](/wiki/File:160316_KL_Monorail_leaving_Raja_Chulan_station_(cropped).jpeg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/KTMB_Class_92_SCS_18_KL_Sentral_Junction.jpg/288px-KTMB_Class_92_SCS_18_KL_Sentral_Junction.jpg)](/wiki/File:KTMB_Class_92_SCS_18_KL_Sentral_Junction.jpg)  
Major urban rail transportation in Kuala Lumpur. Left from top: MRT [Kajang Line](/wiki/Kajang_Line "Kajang Line"), MRT [Putrajaya Line](/wiki/Putrajaya_Line "Putrajaya Line"), LRT [Ampang/Sri Petaling Line](/wiki/Ampang_and_Sri_Petaling_lines "Ampang and Sri Petaling lines"), LRT [Kelana Jaya Line](/wiki/Kelana_Jaya_Line "Kelana Jaya Line"), [KL Monorail Line](/wiki/KL_Monorail_Line "KL Monorail Line") and [KTM Komuter](/wiki/KTM_Komuter "KTM Komuter")

The [KTM Komuter](/wiki/KTM_Komuter "KTM Komuter"), a [commuter rail](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") service, was introduced in 1995 as the first rail transit system to provide local rail services in Kuala Lumpur and the surrounding [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley") suburban areas. Services were later expanded to other parts of Malaysia with the introduction of the [Northern](/wiki/KTM_Komuter_Northern_Sector "KTM Komuter Northern Sector") and Southern sectors.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-197)^ KTM Komuter's 175 km (109 mi) network in the Central Sector has 53 stations. It consists of two cross-city routes, namely the [Port Klang Line](/wiki/Port_Klang_Line "Port Klang Line") ([Tanjung Malim](/wiki/Tanjung_Malim_railway_station "Tanjung Malim railway station") to [Port Klang](/wiki/Port_Klang_Komuter_station "Port Klang Komuter station")) and [Seremban Line](/wiki/Seremban_Line "Seremban Line") ([Batu Caves](/wiki/Batu_Caves_Komuter_station "Batu Caves Komuter station") to [Pulau Sebang/Tampin](/wiki/Pulau_Sebang/Tampin_railway_station "Pulau Sebang/Tampin railway station")). Transfers between the two main lines can be made at any of the four stations on the central core: [KL Sentral](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Sentral "Kuala Lumpur Sentral"), [Kuala Lumpur](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Railway_Station "Kuala Lumpur Railway Station"), [Bank Negara](/wiki/Bank_Negara_Komuter_station "Bank Negara Komuter station") and [Putra](/wiki/Putra_Komuter_station "Putra Komuter station").{#cite_ref-197}

Light Rapid Transit (LRT) Malaysia is the [medium-capacity rail](/wiki/Medium-capacity_rail_system "Medium-capacity rail system") lines in the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley"), [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia"). The first LRT line was opened in 1996 and the system has since expanded to three lines, which opened in 1998 and 1999. Along with the MRT, the LRT is constructed and owned by the Prasarana, with operating concessions currently run by Rapid KL and Rapid Rail. In 2006, the government announced the [Sri Petaling Line](/wiki/Ampang_and_Sri_Petaling_lines_extension "Ampang and Sri Petaling lines extension") and [Kelana Jaya line extension](/wiki/Kelana_Jaya_line_extension "Kelana Jaya line extension") projects.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-198)^ Unlike the original line, which used the fixed-block [signalling block system](/wiki/Signaling_block_system "Signaling block system"), the extension uses the [communications-based train control](/wiki/Communications-based_train_control "Communications-based train control") (CBTC) signalling system.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-199)^^[\[198\]](#cite_note-200)^{#cite_ref-200}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Entrance_B_of_Tun_Razak_Exchange_MRT_station.jpg/220px-Entrance_B_of_Tun_Razak_Exchange_MRT_station.jpg)](/wiki/File:Entrance_B_of_Tun_Razak_Exchange_MRT_station.jpg) Entrance A of the [Tun Razak Exchange MRT station](/wiki/Tun_Razak_Exchange_MRT_station "Tun Razak Exchange MRT station"). The station is designed to look more business-friendly, located in and named after a new [financial district](/wiki/Financial_district "Financial district") under development, [TRX](/wiki/Tun_Razak_Exchange "Tun Razak Exchange").

Mass Rapid Transit (MRT) Malaysia is a heavy rail rapid transit system that constitutes the bulk of the railway network in Kuala Lumpur and the rest of the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley"). The first section of the MRT opened on 16 December 2016, and the network has since grown rapidly following Malaysia's aim of developing a comprehensive rail network as the backbone of the country's public transportation system. The network consists of three lines -- the [13](/wiki/MRT_Circle_Line "MRT Circle Line") [MRT Circle Line](/wiki/MRT_Circle_Line "MRT Circle Line"), looping around Kuala Lumpur, the [9](/wiki/Kajang_line "Kajang line") [MRT Kajang Line](/wiki/MRT_Kajang_Line "MRT Kajang Line") and the [12](/wiki/Putrajaya_line "Putrajaya line") [MRT Putrajaya Line](/wiki/MRT_Putrajaya_Line "MRT Putrajaya Line"), covering a 20 km radius in the southeast--northwest direction from the city centre, will integrate the current [rapid transit](/wiki/Rapid_transit "Rapid transit") system and serve high-density areas which are currently not serviced by any rapid transit system. About 90 new stations are planned in this "wheel and spoke" concept, out of which 26 in the city centre will be underground. Ridership capacity will be two million passengers per day.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}

The [KL Monorail](/wiki/KL_Monorail "KL Monorail") opened on 31 August 2003 with 11 stations running 8.6 km (5 mi) on two parallel elevated tracks. The line is numbered [8](/wiki/KL_Monorail "KL Monorail") and coloured light green on official transit maps. It connects the [KL Sentral](/wiki/KL_Sentral "KL Sentral") transport hub in the south and [Titiwangsa](/wiki/Titiwangsa_station "Titiwangsa station") in the north with the "Golden Triangle", a commercial, shopping, and entertainment area comprising [Bukit Bintang](/wiki/Bukit_Bintang "Bukit Bintang"), Imbi, Sultan Ismail, and Raja Chulan.^[\[200\]](#cite_note-202)^{#cite_ref-202}  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Bandar_Tasik_Selatan_station_%28KLIA_Transit%29%2C_Klang_Valley.jpg/139px-Bandar_Tasik_Selatan_station_%28KLIA_Transit%29%2C_Klang_Valley.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bandar_Tasik_Selatan_station_(KLIA_Transit),_Klang_Valley.jpg)  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Skypark_Link_train_at_Terminal_Skypark_13_Dec_2018.jpg/145px-Skypark_Link_train_at_Terminal_Skypark_13_Dec_2018.jpg)](/wiki/File:Skypark_Link_train_at_Terminal_Skypark_13_Dec_2018.jpg)  
[Airport rail link](/wiki/Airport_rail_link "Airport rail link") in Kuala Lumpur: [ERL](/wiki/Express_Rail_Link "Express Rail Link") (left) and [Skypark Link](/wiki/Skypark_Link "Skypark Link") (right)

Kuala Lumpur is served by two airports. The main airport, [Kuala Lumpur International Airport](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_International_Airport "Kuala Lumpur International Airport") (KLIA) at Sepang, Selangor, which is also the aviation hub of Malaysia, is located about 50 kilometres (31 mi) south of city. The other airport is [Sultan Abdul Aziz Shah Airport](/wiki/Sultan_Abdul_Aziz_Shah_Airport "Sultan Abdul Aziz Shah Airport"), also known as Subang Skypark, and served as the main international gateway to Kuala Lumpur from 1965 until KLIA opened in 1998.

KLIA connects the city with direct flights to destinations on four continents around the world,^[\[201\]](#cite_note-203)^ and is the main hub for the national carrier, [Malaysia Airlines](/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines "Malaysia Airlines") and low-cost carrier, [AirAsia](/wiki/AirAsia "AirAsia"). KLIA can be reached using the [KLIA Ekspres](/wiki/KLIA_Ekspres "KLIA Ekspres"), an [airport rail link](/wiki/Airport_rail_link "Airport rail link") service from [KL Sentral](/wiki/KL_Sentral "KL Sentral"), which takes twenty-eight minutes and costs [RM](/wiki/Malaysian_ringgit "Malaysian ringgit") 55 (roughly US$13.50),^[\[202\]](#cite_note-204)^ while travelling by car or bus via highway will take about an hour but cost a lot less. Direct buses from KLIA to the city centre are plentiful (every 10 to 15 minutes during peak hours), air-conditioned and comfortable with fares ranging from RM 11 (roughly US$2.70) to RM 15 (roughly US$3.70). Air Asia and other low-cost carrier flights do not fly out of KLIA main terminal, but from [KLIA2](/wiki/KLIA2 "KLIA2"), which is two kilometres from KLIA. KLIA2 is served by an extension of the KLIA Ekspres and by a free shuttle bus service from KLIA. As of 2018^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit)^, Sultan Abdul Aziz Shah Airport is only used for chartered and turboprop flights by airlines such as [Firefly](/wiki/Firefly_(airline) "Firefly (airline)") and [Malindo Air](/wiki/Malindo_Air "Malindo Air").^[\[203\]](#cite_note-205)^{#cite_ref-205}  

### Buses {#Buses}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Buses")\]  
Main articles: [Rapid Bus](/wiki/Rapid_Bus "Rapid Bus") and [Kuala Lumpur Mini-Bus Service](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Mini-Bus_Service "Kuala Lumpur Mini-Bus Service")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Volvo_B8L_300.jpg/220px-Volvo_B8L_300.jpg)](/wiki/File:Volvo_B8L_300.jpg) Double-deck buses crossing at [Jalan Ampang](/wiki/Jalan_Ampang "Jalan Ampang")

*Bas Mini KL* or Kuala Lumpur Mini-Bus Service was one of the oldest and most popular [Malaysia](/wiki/Malaysia "Malaysia") [public bus service](/wiki/Public_transportation "Public transportation"), having served Kuala Lumpur and the [Klang Valley](/wiki/Klang_Valley "Klang Valley") region. The buses were primarily painted pink with a white stripe on the sides, and had a capacity of only 20--30 passengers, due to their smaller size. The buses operated on a commission basis, with service operators paid according to the fares they collected. The mini-bus service was from 23 September 1975 and discontinued on 1 July 1998, to be replaced by the Intrakota bus service and later, [Rapid Bus](/wiki/Rapid_Bus "Rapid Bus") in 2005.^[\[204\]](#cite_note-206)^{#cite_ref-206}

Rapid Bus began the first phase of the revamp of its bus network in January 2006, introducing 15 City Shuttle bus routes which serve major areas in the Central Business District (CBD) of Kuala Lumpur. In 2008, Rapid Bus operated 167 routes with 1,400 buses covering 980 residential areas with a ridership of about 400,000 per day.^[\[205\]](#cite_note-207)^ The buses run between four hubs at the edge of the central business district, namely [KL Sentral](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_Sentral_station "Kuala Lumpur Sentral station"), [Titiwangsa](/wiki/Titiwangsa "Titiwangsa"), [Kuala Lumpur City Centre](/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur_City_Centre "Kuala Lumpur City Centre"), [Maluri](/wiki/Maluri_station "Maluri station"), and [Medan Pasar](/wiki/Medan_Pasar_bus_hub "Medan Pasar bus hub") in the city centre. These bus hubs also serve as rail interchanges, with the exception of Medan Pasar, although it is at a walking distance from [Masjid Jamek LRT station](/wiki/Masjid_Jamek_LRT_station "Masjid Jamek LRT station"). On 18 June 2020, [Rapid Bus](/wiki/Rapid_Bus "Rapid Bus") released a new feature: real-time location of bus in [Google Maps](/wiki/Google_Maps "Google Maps"), via collaboration with [Google Transit](/wiki/Google_Transit "Google Transit").^[\[206\]](#cite_note-208)^^[\[207\]](#cite_note-209)^^[\[208\]](#cite_note-210)^^[\[209\]](#cite_note-211)^{#cite_ref-211}

Effective 10 April 2019, all RapidKL buses are implementing a fully cashless journey for all routes by stages, in which the bus accepts [Touch n Go](/wiki/Touch_%27n_Go "Touch 'n Go") cards only for user convenience. These systems were fully implemented by 27 May 2019.^[\[210\]](#cite_note-212)^ Almost 170 RapidKL bus routes are covered with the real-time feature, which was expanded to the MRT feeder bus service. Rapid Bus is however not the only bus operator in Kuala Lumpur and the Klang Valley. Other bus operators are Selangor Omnibus, Setara Jaya Bus, and Causeway Link.{#cite_ref-212}  

### Taxis {#Taxis}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Taxis")\]  
Main article: [Taxicabs of Malaysia](/wiki/Taxicabs_of_Malaysia "Taxicabs of Malaysia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/2010-2013_Proton_Persona_%28CM%29_1.6_sedan%2C_Teksi_%282014-01-03%29.jpg/220px-2010-2013_Proton_Persona_%28CM%29_1.6_sedan%2C_Teksi_%282014-01-03%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:2010-2013_Proton_Persona_(CM)_1.6_sedan,_Teksi_(2014-01-03).jpg) Typical public cab in Kuala Lumpur

In Kuala Lumpur, most taxis have distinctive white and red liveries. Many companies operate and maintain pools of different model of cars in their brands. Before local car production began, the [Mercedes-Benz 200](/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W123 "Mercedes-Benz W123"), [Mazda 323/Ford Laser](/wiki/Mazda_Familia "Mazda Familia"), [Toyota Mark II X80 series](/wiki/Toyota_Mark_II "Toyota Mark II") and the [Opel Kadett](/wiki/Opel_Kadett "Opel Kadett") were used.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-213)^ Most were scrapped and replaced by [Protons](/wiki/List_of_Proton_car_models "List of Proton car models"), but there are still a large number of these models running the roads. Kuala Lumpur is one of the major [ASEAN](/wiki/ASEAN "ASEAN") cities with taxis extensively running on [natural gas](/wiki/Natural_gas_vehicle "Natural gas vehicle"). Taxis can be hailed from [taxi stands](/wiki/Taxicab_stand "Taxicab stand") or from the streets. Taxis may be flagged down at any time of the day along any public road outside of the Central Business District (CBD). However, increased usage of ridesharing services like [Grab](/wiki/Grab_(company) "Grab (company)"), MyCar and JomRides has resulted in a decrease in taxi use.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-214)^{#cite_ref-214}

Nevertheless, the London-based website, LondonCabs.co.uk has claimed that taxis in the city charge passengers high rates, refusing to turn on their meters and offering instead over-priced flat-rate fares,^[\[213\]](#cite_note-215)^ although other passengers contradict such claims. The heads of some taxi associations came out and distanced themselves from taxi drivers who had given the taxi industry a bad name, promising the public that not all taxi drivers were like that.^[\[214\]](#cite_note-216)^{#cite_ref-216}  

Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}
-----------------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Kuala_Lumpur&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities")\]  
See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Malaysia](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Malaysia "List of twin towns and sister cities in Malaysia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Isfahankualalumpur.jpg/150px-Isfahankualalumpur.jpg)](/wiki/File:Isfahankualalumpur.jpg) [Esfahan](/wiki/Isfahan "Isfahan") Street (formerly *Jalan Selat*, Straits Road) in Kuala Lumpur (above) and Kuala Lumpur Avenue in Isfahan (below)

Kuala Lumpur is [twinned](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") with:  
* [Ankara](/wiki/Ankara "Ankara"), Turkey^[\[215\]](#cite_note-217)^{#cite_ref-217}
* [Casablanca](/wiki/Casablanca "Casablanca"), Morocco^[\[216\]](#cite_note-218)^{#cite_ref-218}
* [Chennai](/wiki/Chennai "Chennai"), India^[\[217\]](#cite_note-219)^{#cite_ref-219}
* [Dubai](/wiki/Dubai "Dubai"), United Arab Emirates^[\[218\]](#cite_note-iluminasi-220)^{#cite_ref-iluminasi_220-0}
* [Isfahan](/wiki/Isfahan "Isfahan"), Iran^[\[219\]](#cite_note-221)^{#cite_ref-221}
* [Karachi](/wiki/Karachi "Karachi"), Pakistan^[\[220\]](#cite_note-222)^{#cite_ref-222}
* [London](/wiki/London "London"), United Kingdom^[\[221\]](#cite_note-223)^{#cite_ref-223}
* [Malacca City](/wiki/Malacca_City "Malacca City"), Malaysia^[\[218\]](#cite_note-iluminasi-220)^{#cite_ref-iluminasi_220-1}
* [Mashhad](/wiki/Mashhad "Mashhad"), Iran^[\[222\]](#cite_note-224)^{#cite_ref-224}
